Current Commentary

On the US-Japan Non-Aggression Treaty 21

— Shu

Since President Roosevelt took office in March of last year, dramatic changes have occurred in the politics and economy of the United States. Its foreign policy has also been affected accordingly. The US-Japan relationship is one of the most prominent examples. Since the economic panic in the United States in 1929, domestic industrial equipment has become increasingly dilapidated, and overseas markets have also been sluggish. What has been able to maintain the status quo is entirely due to the subtlety of its diplomatic operations. Even after the September 18th Incident, although the United States repeatedly spoke out for justice, it only stopped at the right point, and it did not want to have more explicit expressions. This is because the United States only focuses on the development of economic interests and the acquisition of sales markets in the Far East. Now the trade relationship between the United States and Japan has reached the first place in the Far East. (Note that US cotton exports to Japan account for half of its national exports. Other items such as machinery, steel, and wood are worth more than 50 million yen per year.) Therefore, the United States will never cut off diplomatic relations with Japan unless it is absolutely necessary and willingly suffer economic losses.

On the Japanese side, although militarists strongly advocate anti-Americanism, their strength to monopolize hegemony in the Pacific is still insufficient. Moreover, raw silk accounts for almost half of Japan's total exports, and the vast majority of raw silk exports go to the United States. Therefore, the conflict between the United States and Japan is definitely not in the interest of Japan's foreign trade. From the perspective of international politics, Japan has tried its best to exert its military aggression policy. Our people certainly have no good feelings about it. Even the Anglo-Japanese relationship is superficial, and the Soviet Union, which dominates the north, is preparing for war to compete with Japan. The conflict and opposition between Japan and the Soviet Union are becoming increasingly acute. If Japan cannot open up a diplomatic outlet in the Pacific, I am afraid that even before the military confrontation, the bloodless economic war alone will be enough to kill it. Therefore, various Japanese propaganda voices for friendship with the United States are singing high into the clouds. First, Hiroshi Saito's lobbying, followed by Fumimaro Konoe's efforts. The negotiation of the so-called US-Japan Non-Aggression Treaty seems to be a step closer to possibility. However, even if the US-Japan Non-Aggression Treaty is concluded, we cannot but doubt whether the peace in the Pacific can be truly maintained. The US-Japan understanding may indeed be sincere in the United States, but Japan has other intentions. Just look at how, after the informal preliminary understanding between the United States and Japan was established, Japan's oppression of the Asian continent has suddenly become more serious. In North China, the number of Japanese troops in Jindong and Malan Pass has suddenly increased to more than 2,000, with many aircraft attached, making the eastern border of Chahar feel very uneasy. Also, in the puppet Manchukuo, the Nagoya Third Division and the Kyoto Sixteenth Division were deployed, carrying a large number of new-style weapons. (Japan still uses the rotation of troops as a cover for this troop deployment. In fact, the combined strength of the Eighth and Tenth Divisions, which were transferred back to the country, is less than two-thirds of the Third and Sixteenth Divisions.) It is preparing to strengthen the international war and covet Inner Mongolia. It can be seen that although the relationship between the United States and Japan is gradually improving, the Asia, then will and

He originally planned to go to the United States when he entered school two years ago, but because there was a temporary parliament, he did not go. Instead, he went on this first trip. This trip to the United States has been rumored to be a goodwill envoy, etc. This kind of goodwill behavior does not seem to be announced in diplomatic strategies. Also, the Hayashi Army Minister issue should not cause a crisis in the political situation, and the Education Minister issue can also proceed smoothly. (14th Den Tsushin Telegram)

(Paris) The French government is about to convene a French colonial economic conference. It has already appointed a committee to draft the agenda and other details. The conference will discuss foreign competition, with particular attention to Japan's advances in Africa, and proposals to ease quotas on and increase production in the colonies. This was planned two years ago, and the decision to convene it has only now been made. French colonial trade has gradually developed over the past decade. If the natural resources of the entire territory are fully developed, France will need to rely on foreign countries for very few products besides oil. (Reuters, 13th)

Page 9

Gold Standard Countries Waver; Italy Implements Major Austerity Measures; Pay Cuts and Rent Reductions to Save Commerce; Export Trade Hit by Japan 29

Rome Today, the cabinet decided on a far-reaching economic plan, hoping to curb Italy's commercial decline. This plan is broad in scope, from pay cuts for civil servants to reductions in rent, presenting a positive austerity trend. Its purpose is to prevent the withdrawal of cash and maintain the country's export trade, in order to resist the benefits gained by the United States, Britain, and Japan due to currency devaluation. This plan is the first austerity step taken by a gold standard country. It is reported that Italy's exports have decreased greatly compared to Japan recently, while Japan's exports have increased greatly in terms of yen, and even in terms of gold, the increase is still considerable. The pay cuts will be progressive, with a 6% reduction for monthly salaries between 500 and 1000 lire, and a 12% reduction for those above 2000. Prime Minister Mussolini will take the largest cut, with the salaries of cabinet members reduced by 20%. Monthly salaries below 500 and the pensions of civil and military personnel will be exempt from cuts. Housing rents will be reduced by 12%, and rents for shops and non-residential buildings will be reduced by 15%. This is the first rent reduction in recent years. The cabinet also decided today that retail food prices should be reduced by 10%. Rumors suggest that wages across the country will also be reduced uniformly. According to official sources, the cost of living in Italy has decreased from 100 to 74 since 1927.

(Reuters, 14th)

British Steel Industry's Five-Year Transformation Plan; Steel Import Tax Over 30%; Trade Subsidies to Restore Exports 30

(London) The British steel industry's five-year reorganization plan was released today. This is an unprecedented major industrial reorganization plan in Britain. The British Empire's steel industry will henceforth be completely controlled by the British Steel Corporation. It is reported that this plan has been approved by the Treasury. It is expected that the measure of collecting an import tax of 33 and 1/3 percent on steel will continue after its expiration in October. This plan authorizes the Steel Industry Association to manage imports by quotas for a period of five years, and to levy a tax on domestic consumption to subsidize export trade in order to restore foreign markets. Its purpose is to eliminate unnecessary competition and encourage the merger of factories and the upgrading of machinery, so that all parts of the British Empire's steel industry can cooperate closely. (Reuters, 13th)

Anglo-Dutch Commercial Negotiations 31

(London) Reuters learned today that the commercial negotiations between Britain and the Netherlands, which are about to begin, do not include the rubber restriction issue, because rubber restriction is a matter for producers of the two countries to discuss, and not within the scope of government negotiations between the two countries. Mussolini Expresses Acceptance of Guarantee Principle; European Map Must Be Remade; Davis to Leave Europe for the United States 32

(New York) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, in an interview with a New York Times correspondent stationed in Rome, stated that the French government, regarding the conclusion of a disarmament convention, advocates that the implementation of guarantees for this convention be a condition for concluding the convention. If the guarantees requested by France are reasonable, then Italy is prepared to accept them in principle. Mussolini went on to discuss Italy's pacifism and expressed satisfaction with the improvement of relations between France and Italy, saying that the relaxation of the European situation is the effect of the signing of the Rome Protocols by Italy, Austria, and Hungary. He then stated that the European map created by the Treaty of Versailles must be remade. If it is not remade by means of war, then it must be remade by other, more appropriate methods. What is this more appropriate method? It is a system of political and economic coordination, proceeding gradually. Finally, Mussolini said that the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference involve too wide a scope, and too many meetings are held. The League of Nations can only exist after all nations have formed good neighborly relations. However, if all nations are to form good neighborly relations, it must first be preceded by the expansion of economic regions. Therefore, the Italian-Austrian-Hungarian Rome Accords are the first step in restoring economic prosperity to the Danube River basin, and also a major undertaking for European peace and reconstruction. This undertaking should be based on the Four-Power Pact and continue to advance. (Havas, 14th)

(London) Davis, the American representative to the Disarmament Conference, recently departed from Waterloo Station to Southampton, where he will board a ship to return to the United States. (Havas, 14th)

Japan Lacks Sincerity Towards Russia in Multilateral Non-Aggression Pact 34

Riga A few days ago, sources in Japan stated that Foreign Minister Hirota was prepared to negotiate a bilateral non-aggression treaty with the United States for a period of ten years or even permanently. However, the United States unofficially indicated that if a mutual non-aggression treaty is to be concluded, it should be jointly concluded by China, the United States, Russia, and Japan, and should not be limited to Japan and the United States. In March of this year, U.S. Secretary of State Hull, in a letter to Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota, also stated that all countries with interests in the Far East should approach problems currently or in the future arising between two or more countries in a spirit of peace and sincerity, which implicitly contains this meaning. Soviet Russian sources believe that Japan's suggestion to the United States to conclude a non-aggression treaty is intended to prevent the United States from interfering in Far Eastern affairs, so that Japan can act freely towards Soviet Russia. The Russian correspondent stationed in Tokyo, in order to ease public sentiment, stated that Japan is not only willing to conclude a non-aggression treaty with the United States, but also with China and Soviet Russia. However, people here still do not believe this news, because when Japanese Ambassador to France Yoshizawa was transferred to the position of Foreign Minister and passed through Moscow on his way home, the Soviet authorities did suggest to him that a Japanese-Russian mutual non-aggression treaty be concluded, but Japan has so far refused this suggestion. (Havas, 13th)

Roosevelt Signs Johnson Act Prohibiting Loans to Defaulting Nations; Enforcing Financial Blockade Against Europe; Aid to Russia Suspended Due to Unsettled Debt 37

(Washington) President Roosevelt signed the Johnson proposal this morning, prohibiting further loans to countries that owe debts, and stipulating that the central government can supervise the raising of debts in the United States by foreign countries. (Reuters, 13th)

(Washington) European countries that have suspended war debt payments to the United States or are only making credit payments will no longer be able to conduct any financial transactions with the United States or sell public bonds. After returning from his cruise, President Roosevelt's first action was to sign the Johnson Act, which effectively imposes a financial boycott on all war debt countries except Finland, because Finland is able to pay each installment of principal and interest on time. The countries subject to the American currency market boycott include Britain, France, Belgium, Poland, Czechoslovakia, Austria, Estonia, Greece, Hungary, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Romania, and Yugoslavia. Several New York bankers are currently willing to purchase European public bonds and recently requested to promote the sale of new French public bonds, but this was ultimately prohibited by Treasury Secretary Morgenthau, on the grounds that the government and Congress have made their attitude towards this move clear in the Johnson Act. Lawyers are currently studying all aspects of the situation related to Soviet Russia. Soviet Russia has not repaid the debts of the Russian Empire and Kerensky. The activities of the Export-Import Bank have been completely suspended pending resolution of legal issues. (Note: The Export-Import Bank is a branch of the Reconstruction Finance Corporation, whose initial intention was to provide financial assistance to American trade with Russia.) It is reported that the proposer of the Johnson Act is Republican Senator Johnson. The bill was initially a reference to a type of wording applied to debtor nations in order to control a majority of countries in Central and South America and Europe. Later, it was revised at the request of the executive authorities. (National Telegram, 13th)

Roosevelt's Situation Upon Arriving in Washington; Humorous Speech to Welcoming Crowd; Claims Two-Week Cruise Has Turned Him Into a Labor-Enduring Oddball 38

(Washington) President Roosevelt returned to Washington today. Two hundred Democratic congressmen lined up at the station to welcome him, led by a naval band. This phenomenon is rarely seen in Washington except when a new president takes office. After shaking hands and thanking each congressman, President Roosevelt gave a brief speech to the crowd, saying, "The journalists accompanying the train have repeatedly asked me to make a statement, expressing their hope for an early adjournment of Congress, but I have not said anything, because I hope you will delay the adjournment, as you wish. I hope that you young people will use my many years of experience to tell me about the advantages of the Washington climate in July and August, where the temperature rarely exceeds 110 degrees and there is absolutely no humidity." This humorous remark caused the audience to burst into laughter. President Roosevelt continued, "Even if I am here all summer, I will not decline. Now I have obtained all

Finally, with a smile, he invited the members of Congress to visit the White House in their free time, saying that he would be willing to share with them some of the whaling skills he had learned. (Reuters, 13th)

Cracks Within Silver Faction 39

(Washington) Cracks caused by the silver issue nearly caused a split among the House leaders today. One faction, led by Lanham, is now working hard to pass several silver regulations before Congress adjourns, while the other faction, led by Congressman Peyser, has received hints from President Roosevelt to adjourn early and has adopted a simple legislative plan to end Congress in mid-May, but without addressing silver. In the House, Lanham is in a position to lead a possible silver rebellion. Lanham published a strong statement in the newspaper today, saying that the opinion of Congress is now working hard to support the passage of the silver bill and will make it happen during this session of Congress. Lanham continued to say that the opinion of Congress is also the opinion of the entire United States. Lanham also attacked the pro-gold faction, accusing them of conspiring to prevent the adoption of silver as currency. Lanham demanded that if the Treasury continues to investigate silver, it should also investigate the activities of the gold faction, and said, "I very much hope that the silver factions in Congress can work together on a single bill," which clearly refers to the mixed silver bill currently being discussed in the Senate. Congressman Fish has obtained 101 signatures on his informal petition seeking timely action by Congress on Fish's silver purchase bill. It is said that the bill may be hindered by the opposition party during this session of Congress, and the opposition party is obstructing the appendix to the bill. The House Banking and Currency Committee has already reported in favor of it. According to observers, if the government is not satisfied with the McCarran Act, then the bill will also have no hope of passing, and the Frazier-Lemke Act, which stipulates the redemption of land deeds at a low price, will also suffer the same result. It is still questionable whether the government's investigation into the trading and storage of silver in New York is part of the government's silver plan, but this secret has aroused a rumor that the government may provide assistance to silver in the future. (National Telegram, 13th)

Proponent of Nationalizing Arms Manufacturing Offers Additional Explanation 40

(Washington) A bill was introduced in the House today stipulating that the manufacture of arms should be changed from private companies to state-owned enterprises. The proponent was Congressman Sirovich, the same person who attacked Japan's secret military plan last Wednesday. Sirovich solemnly stated when proposing the bill that the President has requested property rights to prohibit the shipment of arms to countries that endanger world peace. Regarding this, Sirovich also traced back to the Senate's adoption of the Nye-Vandenberg joint resolution, according to which a special seven-member committee will be established to investigate American arms manufacturing. In his speech, Sirovich said that if this issue is not observed from other perspectives, the easiest feeling is that arms manufacturing should be a state-owned enterprise, because private companies are ultimately influenced by profit. Sirovich further stated that the manufacture of arms should be managed by the government. A reaction occurred in the audience during the speech, saying, "What is the difference between finished arms and unfinished arms? What is the difference between bullets and metal products?" (National Telegram, 13th)

Wave of Strikes Takes Serious Form 41

(Washington) The labor problem is now expanding daily, dealing a major fatal blow to the development of national industry. In Lidotte City, there are currently 5,000 machine model workers who went on strike today. Rumors that the workers are demanding reduced working hours and increased wages have been denied by the workers. Smaller strikes in the city are also underway. The Machine Education Association of Lidotte City has scheduled a meeting on Monday to discuss countermeasures against the general strike of machine workers. The situation of the miners in Pennsylvania is very worrying, as the atmosphere of strikes has become increasingly strong. However, the steel industry is still relatively stable, but workers are demanding pay increases. The oil workers have rejected the terms of the conciliation association, which advocates paying different levels of wages in different regions as a solution. Fleming, president of the International Oil Workers Union, declared today that if this plan of unequal wages is adopted, it will cause 100,000 oil workers to carry out a general strike. (National Telegram, 13th)

Prelude to Soviet Russia Joining the League of Nations; Not Yet at the Stage of Discussing Practical Conditions; Soviet Russia Intends to Be Elected as a Permanent Member of the League of Nations Council 42

(London) Regarding the rumor that Soviet Russia has proposed special conditions for joining the League of Nations, Reuters has learned today that the issue has not yet reached the stage of discussing practical conditions. However, what can be clearly decided now is that Soviet Russia will not be willing to consider suggestions that place it in a secondary position. Soviet Russia now feels that if Britain and France can indicate that Geneva indeed welcomes Soviet Russia, then the minor difficulties of small countries such as Switzerland that do not recognize Soviet Russia can be resolved. (Reuters, 13th)

(London) Although the rumor of Soviet Russia joining the League of Nations has been prevalent in Paris for a while, according to the Daily Mail, the treaty proposed by Soviet Russia for joining the League of Nations is not easy for Britain and other countries to accept, so this matter is still difficult to achieve in the short term. The report also stated that the conditions proposed by Soviet Russia are as follows: (1) All member states of the League of Nations must recognize Soviet Russia; (2) There must be a formal invitation to join the League of Nations; (3) Must be elected as a permanent member of the League of Nations Executive Council. (National Telegram, 13th)

British Union for the League of Nations; Soviet Russian Ambassador Also Attends 43

(London) The United Federation of Associations Supporting the League of Nations held two meetings yesterday. Soviet Russian Ambassador Maisky was present at both meetings. People in the League of Nations believe that this move is of considerable significance. It is said that opinions have recently been exchanged in Geneva on the issue of Soviet Russia joining the League of Nations, and now the Soviet Russian Ambassador has also participated in the United Federation of Associations Supporting the League of Nations. The two events mutually confirm each other, which is quite thought-provoking. Maisky's attendance yesterday shows that Soviet Russia has expressed sympathy for the actions of the Union for the League of Nations in a semi-official form, so his attendance was well-received by the general public. According to some people, if Britain and France express their welcome to Moscow for Soviet Russia to join the League of Nations, then the small countries of the Little Entente, even though they have not yet restored diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia, will not be an obstacle to Soviet Russia's accession to the League. (Havas, 13th)

(London) The United Federation of Associations Supporting the League of Nations continued to meet. Lord Lytton proposed a motion, which was unanimously passed. The motion stated that the international establishment of an agreement to reduce disarmament is essential for maintaining peace and reviving the economy. Lytton also firmly stated that he believes that a universal system of security guarantees is better than a partial system of security guarantees. Postmaster General Wood represented Prime Minister MacDonald and read a letter from the Prime Minister, which said, "The British government recognizes the League of Nations as the foundation of British policy. The British government will continue to encourage and assist cooperation among nations, regardless of its form." Wood also said that telephone communication between Britain and Japan will be possible within this year. (Havas, 13th)

Liu Bandit Has Nowhere to Flee, Encountering Ambushes Everywhere, Suffering Heavy Losses; The Air Force Bombed and Killed Dozens of Bandits in the Zhucheng Area 44

(Jinan) Yesterday afternoon, Liu bandit fled north from Wulian Mountain to Yejigou and Li Xiangchen's brigade, 50 li south of Zhucheng. Li Xiangchen's brigade had already laid an ambush there, and Gao Lantian's regiment also rushed to the scene. Both sides launched a pincer attack, killing more than 50 bandits, capturing more than 40 alive, seizing more than 20 miscellaneous guns, and more than 20 mules and horses. The bandits then fled east to Majiazhuang, where they were intercepted by Xu Wenyao's troops, who captured one Maxim machine gun and killed more than 20 bandits. The bandits then fled southeast to Shengshui, 70 li southeast of the city, which is only 20 li from the coast. Because four warships of the Third Fleet were intercepting them there, they dared not go there and fled northwest again. At 4 pm, they arrived at Changcheng, 25 li north of Zhucheng, and at 7:30 pm, they arrived at Gu County in Gaomi County, 50 li north of Zhucheng, where they were intercepted by Zhang Buyun's troops of the Gaomi County Joint Village Association. As of 7:30 pm, more than 60 bandits and more than 50 bandits' horses had been killed. Fierce fighting was still underway, and the bandits had already collapsed. One regiment of Tang Bangzhi's brigade also launched an attack from Anqiu Jingzhi Town. (14th Dispatch)

(Jinan) Han Fuqu stated that in order to prevent bandits from disturbing the Jiaoji Railway line, he plans to go east to inspect. He was originally scheduled to depart at 5 pm, and the accompanying guards had already boarded the train. However, because the bandits had been defeated, the trip was temporarily cancelled, and only one regiment of the pistol brigade was ordered to go east to suppress the bandits. (14th Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) Xu Kangliang, the leader of the Central Air Force detachment, along with detachment members Jia Chao, Zhou Xiuzhong, and Zhao Jianzhen, each flew bomber aircraft, carrying bombs and machine guns. At 8:30 am on the 14th, they flew from Xu to Lu. Xu and Jia's planes flew around Taohuashan and Ma'ershan, searching for bandit traces without success. They only saw the Lu army pursuing northeast. Xu and Jia then turned northeast and flew to search and reconnoiter the areas of Zhangrishan, Tiechaishan, Niutaishan, Fenghuangshan, and Shengshui. In the area between Mishan and Lishui, 10 li northeast of Zhucheng, they discovered a large force of more than a thousand Liu bandits and horses, who were fleeing northwest at a very fast pace, divided into a dozen teams. When they saw the planes arrive, they scattered in panic. Xu and Jia then dropped eight heavy bombs, killing dozens of bandits and dozens of horses. This place was already more than a hundred li away from the Lu army's pursuing troops. Because Xu and Jia had insufficient gasoline, they could not fly low to strafe with machine guns, so they immediately turned back. On the way, they encountered Sun Tonggang's plane and guided it to Zhucheng to drop bombs, and dropped a communication bag in Zhucheng, instructing them to defend against Liu bandit's attack on the city. They then returned to Linyi to refuel. At 3 pm, Zhou and Zhao arrived in Xuzhou. Zhou and Zhao flew again to the bandit area in the afternoon to drop bombs, bombing and killing forty to fifty bandits. They returned to Xuzhou that night. According to Xu, on the night of the 13th, Liu bandit broke through the Lu army's heavy encirclement from Taohuashan and fled fiercely north, advancing more than a hundred li overnight. Chairman Han of Shandong Province originally planned to use heavy troops to divide into three fronts, northwest, south, and east, to encircle Liu bandit, press towards the Rizhao coast, drive them to the coast, and annihilate them in one fell swoop. Therefore, Liu bandit desperately rushed out from the north and fled to Zhucheng again. If the military strength on the Jiaoji Road is weak, Liu bandit will probably flee to Jiaodong. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Qingdao) At about 8 am on the 14th, a naval plane, piloted by Chief Feng and others, went to the Wangdian area west of the sea to reconnoiter, but found no bandit traces. They also flew to Shijiusuo, but found no bandit traces either. They returned to Qing at about 11 am. The Municipal Hospital dispatched Director of Internal Medicine He Shinian and others to Hongshiya to treat the defending soldiers. (14th Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) Xu Kangliang flew a plane on the 14th to reconnoiter and bomb Liu bandit, and observed that the bandit troops broke through the encirclement from Taohuashan Ma'ershan in the evening and fled north, reaching the area between Mishan and Lishui north of Zhucheng, and fled north, seemingly trying to cross the Jiaoji Railway line and flee north. He has already reported to the Three Armies Headquarters, and telegraphed Shandong to strictly guard against it and not allow them to cross the road. (14th Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) Two central bomber planes flew to eastern Shandong again on the morning of the 14th to reconnoiter and saw that Liu bandit had fled to the area between Mishan and Lishui, 10 li north of Zhucheng, with about a thousand cavalry, who were fleeing northwest. They then dropped eight heavy bombs, killing dozens of bandits. At that time, the Lu army's pursuing troops were quite far from the bandits, so they dropped a communication bag in Zhucheng, instructing them to strictly guard against it. On the way back, they encountered Sun Tonggang flying east in a plane, and guided him to the bandit area to bomb. They returned to Xuzhou in the evening. (14th Dispatch)

(Jinan) Chen Dexin's brigade in Jiaoxian and the directly subordinate troops of the 29th Division in Zhoucun disembarked at Caijiazhuang, Gaomi, and went south to suppress the bandits. (14th Dispatch)

The Japanese Military Department Attempts to Interfere in Politics Again; The Saito Cabinet Is Unstable and Uneasy; It Will Take the Opportunity of Recommending a New Army Minister to Force the Government to Implement Extraordinary National Policies 66

(Tokyo) If the successor of Army Minister Hayashi is realized early, it is worthy of attention what policies the top leadership of the army will adopt towards the government. However, it is believed that they will be attached to certain conditions. Although the content is still unclear, it is generally to solve the extraordinary situation proposed by Army Minister Araki after the May 15th Incident. It is necessary to establish thorough work in all departments at home and abroad, and implement it as soon as possible as a prerequisite. The specific items include establishing a proactive and thorough national defense policy that focuses on solving the Manchurian problem, thoroughly implementing the organization and integrity, and thoroughly implementing ideological and educational countermeasures and rural countermeasures. However, since the establishment of the current cabinet, successive army ministers have repeatedly proposed these issues, and the government has also recognized them, but their actions are extremely mild and slow. If this situation continues in the future, there is a risk of causing serious consequences. Therefore, it is advocated that the government must be awakened to this point. The atmosphere among young officers is even stronger, so the trend of the problem is quite significant. (14th Dentsu Dispatch)

(Tokyo) After Sadao Araki resigned as Army Minister, the power of the military department suddenly declined. However, this is only a temporary phenomenon, and the financial groups and political parties have been able to take advantage of this opportunity to vigorously suppress the military department. The timing they hoped for was the 65th session of the Diet and the cabinet meeting after the Diet, and the following principles for foreign affairs and Manchuria were determined: (1) To condemn the military department's warmongering and to restrain its hasty and reckless policies of aggression against the United States, Russia, and North China. (2) To oppose the Kwantung Army's conspiracy to seize the full power to govern Manchuria. The Kwantung Army had to agree to reduce the organization of its special affairs department recently, and all policies towards Manchuria still belong to the control of the central government. (3) The financial groups' free investment in Manchuria is not restricted by the Kwantung Army. (4) The Kwantung Office governs the Manchurian Railway Attached Lands, and criticizes the Kwantung Army's claim to govern the puppet organization. It also took advantage of the opportunity of Zheng Xi and the two traitors visiting Japan to consolidate its policy principles regarding Manchuria. However, Army Minister Hayashi did nothing, and the young officers of the military department were extremely indignant. Army Minister Hayashi felt the heavy responsibility and proposed his resignation. The military department's anger towards the political parties and financial groups then turned to the Saito Cabinet, believing that the current cabinet could not assume the important political task of the extraordinary situation, and would take advantage of Army Minister Hayashi's resignation to demand that Prime Minister Saito earnestly implement the military department's policies, otherwise it would threaten with the so-called "final awakening of the military department." The fate of the Saito Cabinet is like a candle in the wind. (14th Hualian Dispatch)

Winter Arrives in Antarctica; The Long Polar Night; Sunlight Will Not Be Seen Again for Seven Months 73

Little America (Antarctica) The Antarctic winter will begin today. In another eight days, all of Antarctica will turn into darkness. After a long period of darkness, sunlight will not shine there again until next spring. Rear Admiral Richard Byrd of the Antarctic Expedition and all 55 members of the team will stay in the built huts to spend this long and cold winter, stopping outdoor expeditions. Byrd has moved all the expedition books and equipment into the room, and the radio is also inside to engage in indoor research. After seven months, sunlight will be seen again. (13th Kuomintang Dispatch)

Fu Sinian Talks About Excavation Work 75

(Nanjing) Fu Sinian, Director of the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica, said that the object of our excavation work is ruins, places where ancient people lived that have academic research value. Modern countries attach great importance to them. As for ancient tombs, they are protected and cannot be excavated. Even if ancient tombs are occasionally encountered during the excavation of ruins, they are only moved to other places and not damaged. Some unscrupulous elements among antique dealers use the name of excavation to excavate ancient tombs without authorization. The government has ordered a ban. Cotton and Wheat 78

New York Cotton Today (April 14) The cotton market opened with mixed feelings. Bulls closed positions, and the South, New Orleans, and local areas all sold out, while traders, spot merchants, bankers, and Japanese merchants bought in. The market conditions were bleak before noon, and there were not many transactions. Later, due to the good news that the consumption volume in March reached 544,000 bales, the price rose slightly.

Bombay Cotton The Bombay cotton market fell today (April 14) due to sales by European exporters and Japanese merchants. The opening price of white Locke cotton for the July-August period was two hundred and two rupees and seventy-five, a decrease of two and a half rupees.

Liverpool Cotton The Liverpool cotton market today (April 14) The price for the July period opened at 5.97, a decrease of five pounds from yesterday.

Liverpool Wheat The Liverpool wheat market today (April 14) The closing price for the July period was four shillings and five and a half pence, a decrease of half a pence from yesterday's price.

Rubber 79

London Today (April 14) The London rubber market conditions were stable. The trading price for the July-September period at noon was quiet, and the price was also loose, because the Dutch government's proposal to the United Kingdom to restrict the method was denied.

Hongsheng Foreign Firm received a telegram from London stating that, according to the London Financial Times's New York visit telegram, the total amount of copper reserves decreased by 45 million pounds in March. US reserves decreased by 35 million pounds, and foreign reserves decreased by 10 million pounds. The current reserves are a total of 118.2 million pounds, of which 98.8 million pounds are in the United States and the remaining 19.4 million pounds are abroad. The US consumption volume was 85 million pounds, and the foreign consumption volume was 16.9 million pounds. This is one of the largest consumption volumes in recent years.

The Saito Cabinet Like a Tumbler (Japanese Communication) The Reason Why Saito Can Continue Numerous Internal Contradictions of the Warlords 102

During the 65th Diet session, the Saito Cabinet repeatedly faced dangerous situations. In principle, it should have long since ceased to exist. Araki's resignation can be interpreted as the Japanese military has always been independent of the government, and does not involve the entire cabinet, which is possible. However, the Minister of Commerce and the Minister of Education, both important cabinet members, were forced to resign at the same time due to so-called disciplinary issues, yet the cabinet still exists. This is considered strange by most Japanese people. The reasons why Saito can maintain his position are: First, the struggle between the warlords and the financial groups has not yet resulted in a clear victory or defeat. Although the army can use force to seize power, it can no longer take actions like the May 15th Incident, or even more violent actions, to completely concentrate power in the hands of the warlords by inciting so-called extraordinary incidents. Second, the financial groups can only passively conserve and cannot take active offensive actions. In other words, they can only maintain the shell of parliamentary politics and cannot revive the spirit of parliamentary politics. Third, under the current situation, it is impossible to find a person more suitable and more able to mediate between the warlords and the financial groups than Saito Makoto. Because several candidates for prime minister, in terms of personal relationships and general political views, are either biased towards the military or come from political parties, and they would inevitably offend one side of the warlords and the financial groups. As a result, none of them can come to power. The only option is to let Saito continue.

After the 65th Diet session ended, the life of the Saito Cabinet was no longer in the hands of the Diet, but decided by Prince Saionji Kinmochi, the elder statesman sitting in Oiso. When Saito visited Saionji, he expressed his own opinion that he could continue. Saionji also advocated that he continue and persuaded him to make it difficult for himself. Because Saionji still adhered to his theory of constitutional normalcy, in other words, he did not approve of the warlords' dictatorship, and of course, he opposed overthrowing the constitution. Therefore, in Saionji's view, overthrowing the Saito Cabinet and having Araki come to power was absolutely inappropriate. Therefore, the Saito Cabinet must consider how to implement proactive policies and how to supplement the practical issues of the Minister of Education.

The so-called proactive policies roughly consist of two major aspects: First, we are now facing the international crisis of 1936. The Washington Naval Treaty is expiring, and Japan will formally withdraw from the League of Nations from that time onward. At the same time, there are various problems between Anglo-Japanese relations and the Soviet Union. How should these matters be dealt with? Second, the "Manchukuo" puppet state has already had two puppets who have come to the East, and the entire Japanese nation has been playing with them for a while. But how to promote the economy, to put it bluntly, is how to economically control the four northeastern provinces. The answer to the former question is to start with diplomacy, especially with the United States. It is now cracking down on all writings that promote the Japanese-American War or oppose the United States too strongly. In addition to Saito Hiroshi, the ambassador to the United States, exerting diplomatic ability, it recently dispatched the rising aristocrat politician Konoe Fumimaro to the United States to lobby, in order to improve Japanese-American relations and reduce its maritime concerns. The economic control of Manchuria is actually just playing tricks on the puppets at most, and it does not hinder Japan's policies. The most important thing now is still the struggle between the warlords and the financial groups. For example, the reorganization of the South Manchuria Railway Company not only affects the Manchurian economy but also involves politics. Judging from the current situation, it will be difficult for the Japanese faction to completely control Manchuria with the warlords and make the financial groups their appendages. In fact, there will probably be many difficulties, and the result will probably be a different way. However, economic annexation of Manchuria is inevitable.

On the other hand, there are also domestic problems in Japan, namely, reforming the fundamental policies of education, rice countermeasures, and measures to rectify discipline. Regarding education, because the general ideology in Japan has recently deteriorated, whether to the left or to the right, it tends to be illegally extreme. Assassination conspiracies continue to occur, which often shakes society. Left-leaning thought is enough to shake its upper class and create a phenomenon of terror. Therefore, the Japanese government must have a policy of appeasement. As for the rice problem, it has been debated many times in the Diet, in cabinet meetings, and in general forums. The only result that can be implemented is the government's method of buying up and stockpiling. The so-called rectification of discipline is a matter of morality and probably will not have any major effect on Japan's actual politics. (April 7 in Tokyo)

Liu Bandit Heavily Wounded in Jiaoxian There are Rumors That Liu Himself Was Injured 103

Qingdao Communication: After the remnant bandit Liu Guitang crossed the border into Shandong for the second time, Han Fuju, Chairman of Shandong Province, specially dispatched a large army of 400 to encircle and suppress them. Although there have been repeated victories, because the bandits are all fierce and some foreigners are secretly helping and assisting them, they have not been completely eliminated immediately. It is now reported that Liu's bandits have been repeatedly encircled and suppressed by the Shandong army and have been reduced to smaller groups. One group fled into the territory of Mengyin, and another group of about 500 mounted bandits fled north through Yuligou, Juxian County, to the Qishan Town in Anqiu County. Another group went east, crossed Zhucheng and entered Wangtai Town in Jiaoxian County, and near Hongshiya in the Haixi District of Qingdao. The Zuoshan and Huangqibao stations on the Jiaoji Railway are close to Anqiu, and defense has become particularly tight. After receiving the report, the Jiaolu Bureau specially sent Police Chief Dai Shihan with three platoons of road police on a special train west at 2 a.m. today (the 11th) to consolidate road defense to ensure safety. The Qingdao Municipal Government is also deeply concerned that Liu's bandits will affect the city's security. The Qingdao Navy also specially dispatched two bombers today to scout Liu's bandits' actions. It flew again once in the afternoon to scout, but still did not get any trace of Liu's bandits. All the aircraft have now returned to Qingdao and will continue to scout tomorrow. It is also reported that there are about 500 bandits who have entered Jiaoxian County. The battle was fierce, and Liu's bandits suffered heavy casualties. Liu Guitang himself was seriously injured. There were many foreigners under Liu's command, and they are now being closely investigated under the protection of foreigners. If there are suspicious people, they will be taken to the bureau for interrogation. (12th)

Northwest Inspection Record by Our Newspaper's Special Correspondent, Geng Ya 105

Geng Ya's Xinjiang Inspection Record is now renamed Northwest Inspection Record. The reasons are: (1) Before Geng Ya set off, he telegraphed Chairman Sheng of Xinjiang. Yesterday, he received a telegram from Chairman Sheng stating that bandits were showing their full strength, and they are currently being pursued. Fearing there would be danger, he instructed Geng Ya to postpone his trip. However, Geng Ya had already set off and arrived in Datong. Therefore, he was telegraphed to turn west and inspect Shaanxi and Gansu. However, when the telegram arrived in Datong, Geng Ya had already gone to Suiyuan. Another telegram was sent to Suiyuan, but he had already left for another place. It is still unknown whether he will receive it. (2) The name is the same as Feng Youzhen's Xinjiang Inspection Record, which will be published soon. To avoid misunderstanding, the name has been changed. Please forgive the readers.

To Zhangjiakou 106

On April 1st, at 10:00 AM, I departed from Pingxi and arrived at the Pingsui Railway Station outside Xizhimen. More than ten policemen were busily sweeping and cleaning, presenting a particularly tense scene. Upon inquiry, I learned that it was part of the official work for the "National Railway Hygiene Movement Conference." Entering the station, ticket buyers lined up in order of arrival. Apart from those who had already entered the platform, there were thirty-four people waiting in line to buy tickets, without any crowding or clamor. Those carrying heavy luggage could place it beside the queue, with the police taking care of it and the owners keeping an eye on it, so that it would not be confused or lost. Women or soldiers, even if they arrived later, were allowed to buy tickets out of turn. In reality, most soldiers traveled by presenting their passports without buying tickets, and those who did buy tickets were usually accompanied by family members. Other service personnel, such as those at the "weighing scale," "luggage check-in," "information desk," and "ticket inspectors," were mostly able to fully provide convenience to passengers and merchants in various aspects without harming the interests of the railway bureau. I had previously heard that the tracks of the Pingsui Railway were old and dilapidated, and that the revenue was poor, so I expected the services to be casual. However, upon seeing this situation, I was quite surprised. In particular, the orderly maintenance by the police and the orderly ticket-buying process were indeed good phenomena not found on other railways. "If you hold an axe to hew an axe-handle, the pattern is not far off." Are those responsible for maintaining order on other railways interested in this?

Recently, in order to support the development and exploitation of agriculture and industry in the Northwest, and to facilitate passengers and merchants, the Pingsui Railway Bureau has added two additional trips to the three weekly special express trains to Baotou. These trains transport grain and miscellaneous goods eastward, and export tea westward. The freight rates for tea, brick tea, and tea dust have all been specially reduced. As a result, merchants can travel more conveniently, and the railway's revenue has also increased. The entire length of the railway is over 800 kilometers. In the years of 1924 and 1925, the annual revenue was over 11 million yuan. Later, due to the impact of wars and frequent disasters, the annual revenue gradually decreased, almost to the point of bankruptcy. However, in 1933, the revenue suddenly increased to 9.09 million yuan, and the prospect of recovery is quite promising. It is said that the Director, Shen Chang, has already drafted a recovery plan. For construction, the first priority is to replace the sleepers. Most of the 1.53 million sleepers on the entire line have long exceeded their service life, and at least 363,500 sleepers should be replaced. The second priority is to purchase steel beams and steel rails. For machinery, the priorities are to install air brakes, purchase locomotive and vehicle parts, and expand the repair shops. For operations, the priorities are to establish long-distance telephone lines and electrical railway signal systems. In total, the construction, machinery, and operations departments will require more than 2.55 million yuan. Furthermore, due to the steep and dangerous slope of the Guanggou section, a special situation (details below), there is also a proposal to change the route. The new route has already been surveyed. It is longer than the old route, and the project is huge, so it may not be easy to realize.

At 11:00 AM, the bell rang and the train departed. It consisted of twelve cars, including one first-class car. The passengers in the third-class cars were more crowded. After the ticket inspection, I learned the reasons. First, soldiers with passports could ride in first class. Second, it was the school vacation season, and there were many students traveling. Third, family members of soldiers and merchants who frequently traveled, even though they only had third-class tickets, used the excuse that the third-class cars were too crowded and sat down in the first-class cars. Therefore, there were few actual first-class ticket buyers, but many people vying for seats in the first-class car. At Qinghuayuan Station, Tsinghua University was in sight. At Changping Station, I saw more than twenty small donkeys with saddles, led by donkey drivers, vying to pick up passengers. No one got off the train, so everyone squatted down to watch the wheels of the train move forward again. The city is more than ten miles from the station. The broken and incomplete walls of the city can be vaguely seen between the dark yellow willow branches.

Nankou Station has a railway locomotive factory. The tracks are complex, with large and small locomotives arranged in a variety of ways, all with their fires lit and ready to go. Small locomotives use five or seven pairs of wheels and are used for traveling on flat roads. Large locomotives use ten or fourteen pairs of wheels. The size and power of the machinery are twice as great as those of small locomotives. From here onwards, the slope begins, and the small locomotive is replaced with a large one. When we arrived, the train had twelve cars, half of which were detached. Six cars went first, with the large locomotive at the rear, pushing with force. Leaving the station, I first saw the "Monument to the Martyrs of the National Army's Nankou Battle," which was more than thirty feet tall and could be seen from dozens of miles away. It was built by Feng Yuxiang. Not five miles further, the train entered the steep mountain pass of thousands of feet, slowly ascending. The slope at Dongyuan Station became steeper and steeper, going up and down again. The fire was fully stoked, and the train began to climb again. I heard that the locomotive at the rear required twice the fire power as one at the front. However, if the locomotive was at the front, there was a risk that the rear cars would be pulled off and break, causing a great danger. Passing through the Juyongguan tunnel, the Great Wall wound along the top, forming a dangerous terrain. One can imagine the value of "one man guarding the pass, ten thousand men cannot pass" in the old days. In the past, the Zhili-Fengtian Allied Forces defeated the National Army at Nankou. The National Army had retreated for two days, but the Allied Forces still bombarded them without daring to pursue, because of the fearsome natural barrier. Passing through another tunnel, we arrived at Qinglongqiao. A bronze statue of Zhan Tianyou, the founder of the railway, stood at the station. Dozens of male and female college students traveling were resting on the winding Great Wall. Among them, pairs of men and women left the group and went elsewhere, either playing with stones by the stream or talking under the pine trees, which was quite enjoyable.

The journey from Nankou to Qinglongqiao took three quarters of an hour. From here onwards, the road gradually became lower and flatter. The locomotive was changed to a small one. The climate also seemed colder. The ice in the streams was thickly accumulated and had not yet melted. The spring scenery of tender yellow willow branches and slightly green grass in the plains was no longer visible. Passing through the Badaling tunnel took five minutes. Outside the tunnel was a small town with solid buildings, but it was desolate and terrifying. Kangzhuang was all flat land. The train stopped for half an hour, waiting to pick up the remaining cars that had been left at Nankou, and then set off together. Huailai City relied on the mountain slopes and possessed a strategic advantage. Feng Zhanhai's army of 17,000 men was stationed in the city. Hsiahuayuan had a line of poles like telegraph poles, coming from the distant mountains. I heard that it was a coal transport mechanism. It was a pity that I could not see it in operation. The ice on the river beside the road gradually melted, and the Huangshui River rushed rapidly, sometimes splashing waves on the sand surface, sometimes flowing secretly under the ice. The ice blocks collided with each other, making a clanging sound. There was little soil, sand, gravel, grass, or trees. At dusk, the smoke from cooking fires rose everywhere, and the cold air attacked. There were many grains transported eastward at each station, indicating the abundance of products in the Northwest.

There were five Russians in my carriage. I heard that they were managers of the Dehua Trading Company in Zhangjiakou. Zhangjiakou, along with Dolon and Guihua, was opened as a commercial port in 1914, and commerce has been increasing and developing ever since. The primary destination for its import and export goods is Kulun, followed by Dolon. During the Kulun Incident in 1929, the capital of Chinese merchants in that area, some with 100 to 200 thousand yuan, was completely confiscated, totaling more than tens of millions of yuan. People wanted to return, but it was difficult. Since the transportation was cut off, our commercial relations were terminated. Initially, the Russians had established the Xihai Company in Zhangjiakou. Later, due to the severance of relations between China and Russia, it was renamed Dehua Trading Company, which monopolized the trade between Kulun and Zhangjiakou. The imports were mushrooms, crystals, furs, etc., and the exports were tea. The annual business was about seven to eight million yuan. After the resumption of relations between China and Russia, its activities became even more vigorous. Chinese merchants wanted to restore trade relations with Kulun, but it was ineffective to negotiate directly with Kulun. When they turned to negotiate with the Soviet Union, they were told that the authority was not there. This has been delayed until now. Furthermore, Dolon has been captured by the Japanese puppets, and the commerce in Zhangjiakou has fallen sharply. Merchants in Zhangjiakou are privately discussing and all want to request the government to find ways to remedy the situation. It was already 9:00 PM when the train arrived in Zhangjiakou. Hotel staff holding paper lanterns lined up outside the station to greet passengers. I got off the train and stayed at the New Hotel.

Liu Xiang Telephones about the Suppression of Bandits in Tongjiang; All Sichuan Army Units Achieve Great Victories; Also Describes the General Situation of the Three-Phase Military Operations 107

Chengdu Dispatch: Since the Sichuan Army began its full-scale bandit suppression in October of last year, it has successively recovered the areas of Zhaohua, Guangyuan, Jian'ge, Langzhong, Cangxi, Nanchong, Yingxian, Peng'an, Yilong, Qu County, Xuanhan, Dachuan, Wanxian, Banan County, and Nanyue County, totaling fifteen counties. Among them, the seven counties of Nanba, Yingxian, Yilong, Xuanhan, Dachuan, Wanxian, and Nanba were completely occupied by the bandits, while eight-tenths of the areas of the remaining nine counties were occupied by the bandits. More than 230,000 troops were mobilized. The strength of the bandits, excluding guerrilla units and special detachments, consisted of twenty-six divisions in eight regular Red Army corps, with a total strength of more than 150,000 troops. The total number of bandit deaths and injuries exceeded 80,000. The total number of people killed by the bandits was approximately one million. The tragic sacrifice was unparalleled in three hundred years, except for Zhang Xianzhong's devastation of Sichuan. Fortunately, the bandit suppression armies were extremely diligent, and the people also cooperated effectively with the government troops, striving forward together. Currently, only Tongjiang County has not been recovered, and only 60 to 70 thousand bandits remain. It may not be difficult to completely eliminate them in the short term. On the 9th, Liu Xiang reported the bandit suppression situation and recent victories to various parties, stating: "Since the issuance of the third-phase general offensive order, the progress of each unit in the entire Sichuan bandit suppression situation is as follows: (1) The main force of the Red Bandits is still concentrated in the Five Roads area. The main figures of the bandits, from the puppet chairman Zhang Guotao, the puppet Fourth Front Army commander Xu Xiangqian, the puppet General Political Department Director Chen Changhao, and the puppet Sichuan-Shaanxi Province Chairman Xiong Guobing, downwards, are all supervising the battle in this area. Recently, the bandit forces have heavily fortified this area, which is also based on high mountains and broken cliffs, extremely dangerous. Our Five Roads Army has launched repeated fierce attacks, suffering thousands of casualties, and initially made very little progress. The bandits then took advantage of the windy and rainy nights to attack from time to time. Later, we changed our strategy, extracting a portion of our forces to launch a surprise attack on Wanyuan from the right flank, catching the bandits off guard. Fortunately, we occupied it, allowing the frontal assault to fully connect quickly. The Liao unit of the Six Roads Army launched another full-line attack on the 2nd and 3rd, fighting hard all night, enduring extreme hardships. The bandit units were unable to withstand the pressure and gradually wavered. For three days and nights, our Five Roads Army finally destroyed and seized the most dangerous strongholds on the bandit's front, such as the Honglingtai, Guanzishan, Maoping, and Baihezhai. Thereupon, the entire line separately bypassed and charged in, and on the 4th, we occupied the Shilon Township, Nilong Township, Luming Township, Qiujiabao, Tudibao, Yankou Township, Chenghuangmiao, Yanshan Township, Ba Township, Luowenba, and other places. The bandits collapsed, and we captured, killed, and wounded more than 2,000 people. In total, the bandit's front was more than 200 li long, and we had been in a stalemate for more than a month. Now, in just a few days, we have completely occupied this mountain range, relying entirely on the central government's prestige and the soldiers' united willingness to die. Only then were we able to achieve this success. On the 5th and 6th, our army bravely attacked again, occupying places such as Xiaolao Guanmiao, Sihe Tan, Qubinkou, Guanyin Township, and Zhenshi Township. On the 7th and 8th, we occupied Wenfeng Mountain, Gaoqiao, Tumen Township, Liuping, Changtan River, Longbei Township, and Jigongzhai. Our front line is now only forty li away from Tongjiang City. The bandits have now all gathered in Tongjiang City, intending to defend it to the death. We have dispatched three teams of aircraft to bomb the city daily, and our large army is continuing its fierce advance, forming an encirclement. Tongjiang will not be difficult to recover in the short term. (2) The Deng Army of the One Roads Army advanced from the northern route, capturing Changchi on the 2nd. The most important terrain in that area is Changchi, which is the highest point. Southwards towards Nanjiang, it is all downhill. The bandit strength in this area is also weaker. With the advantage of both manpower and terrain, and the army's renewed efforts, we captured Nanjiang on the 7th. The Tian unit of the Two Roads Army, coordinating with the One Roads Army, also recovered Baimiao Ao and Xindianzi. (3) The Li-Luo unit of the Three Roads Army attacked Bazhong and is now attacking from the flanks, engaging the bandits in fierce battles. We have already occupied Shitang Township and are advancing towards Qingjiang Ferry. (4) The Yang Army of the Four Roads Army is hampered by the Jiangkou River and the dangerous mountain terrain. Repeated attacks have not been successful. However, the Five Roads Army on the left flank and the Three Roads Army on the right flank are advancing and outflanking them, and they have already made contact. Progress must be made in the coming days. (5) The strategic direction of this bandit suppression is to encircle and annihilate them, preventing them from harassing neighboring regions and harming the country. Currently, the right flank has occupied Wanyuan, and the left flank has occupied Nanba. Although the central area is advancing more slowly, in terms of the overall situation, the encirclement has been formed. Each unit is continuing to advance fiercely in unison. The bandits are facing enemies on all sides and will find it difficult to resist. This is the general situation of the recent offensive and defensive situation. The Red Bandits have been disturbing Sichuan for more than a year, devastating as many as sixteen counties. The disaster is worse than floods and ferocious beasts. Fortunately, the military and civilians are united and working with sincerity, so there has been such an effect today. However, the great sacrifices made before and after can be imagined. In addition to reporting to the central government, I am sending this detailed report. Liu Xiang, green seal." (April 10th, Guowen News Agency)

Wuxi Department of Construction to Implement Factory Inspections 114

The Jiangsu Department of Construction previously received an order from the Ministry of Industry to implement factory inspections. The Central Factory Inspection Office also sent personnel to assist in the process. Director Shen believes that factory inspection is an important policy to improve factory management and labor conditions, and to develop industrial production. Countries around the world have implemented it successively, but China has not yet done so. The Shanghai Municipal Government previously used the fact that Jiangsu Province had not yet implemented factory inspections as an excuse to demand the right to inspect factories in the concessions. Therefore, the inspection work in Jiangsu Province cannot be delayed any longer. Recently, the central government promulgated the Implementation Procedures for Factory Inspections, dividing the process into five phases, each lasting fifteen years, adopting a gradual approach as the standard for implementation. However, at this initial stage of implementation, cooperation with local authorities is essential. Therefore, the Factory Inspector of this department, Cheng Qiyuan, has been specially dispatched to Wuxi to prepare for the work by conducting preliminary inspections. Wuxi has a large number of factories, the most of any county in inland Jiangsu Province, and the inspection procedures are extremely complicated. It is feared that there may be other obstacles and difficulties. Therefore, the Chamber of Commerce is being requested in advance to assist in the process. It is also heard that Committee Member Cheng is scheduled to arrive in Wuxi on the 17th. The county government has decided to invite representatives from the Chamber of Commerce and factory managers to a meeting to discuss the implementation of the inspection and clarify its intentions, so as to avoid various misunderstandings.

Additional Construction Fee on Salt 116

After the National Government promulgated the new Salt Law last year, the main principle was to build warehouses to consolidate salt production in each area into warehouses. Recently, the Ministry of Finance issued a special order to the Songjiang Salt Transport Deputy Office to comply with the matter of adding a construction fee to each salt field. The office printed and issued a public notice stating that, starting from April 11th, a construction fee of one jiao would be added to each dan of refined salt or coarse salt. The local Salt Public Company has also received the above-mentioned order and immediately notified all salt merchants to comply. After receiving the order, the wine and soy sauce industries in the county, due to the recent sharp rise in the price of foreign goods, decided to increase the price of salt by one wen per jin starting today (the 15th). The public notice of the Songjiang Salt Transport Deputy Envoy's Office is recorded as follows: "On April 7th of this year, we received the following telegram from the Ministry of Finance: Songjiang Transport Deputy Officer, regarding the collection fee of one jiao for warehouse construction in your area, the proposed methods for collection, storage, and expenditure have been reviewed and approved. It is hereby ordered that collection should begin in your area from April 11th. You should comply with this order. We have also previously received an order from the Ministry stating that all salt sold in the territory of your area, whether refined or coarse salt, should be subject to the construction fee." We should comply with the order. All counties under the jurisdiction of this district, as well as Langxi County in Anhui, and Baoshan Jieyi Jiushang Nanchuan, Shanghai Concession, Chongqi Changyinsha, Hengsha Islands, and various special districts, as well as various refined salt companies, which transport and sell refined salt to the commercial ports of this district, should comply with the order to increase the price by one jiao per dan (i.e., one li per jin) starting from April 11th for both refined salt and soy sauce. In addition to notifying the Salt Merchant Association in the Five Districts of Suzhou, a special telegram has been sent to salt stations in various locations to comply with the order. This public notice is issued for the compliance of all merchants and residents in the sales areas."

Verdict in the Xie Sheng Arson Case 117

On the late evening of January 3rd of this year, the Xie Sheng Silk Store on Daishi Bridge suddenly caught fire, spreading to neighboring stores and households, causing losses of over 100,000 yuan. The manager of the silk store, Fan Wenjing, and the insurance broker, Su Jinchu, were suspected of instigating arson and were detained and sent to court for interrogation. After the Prosecutor's Office completed its investigation, it filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 187, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, which deals with endangering public safety. Judge Liu Bingyu summoned witnesses for separate hearings five times. However, the case was complex and difficult to conclude quickly. On the 12th of this month, Judge Liu again held a public hearing with more than ten people related to the case. Fan hired lawyer Xiang Binghu to appear in court as his defense, and Su hired lawyer Zhang Tong as his defense. The court hearing lasted for a long time before the arguments were declared closed and the verdict was scheduled to be announced on the 14th. Fan and Su were returned to custody, and Zhang Renshan was released on his original bail. Yesterday (the 14th) at 10:00 AM, the sentence was announced. Judge Liu summoned the detained Fan and Su to the court and read out the main text of the judgment. Fan Jingwen was sentenced to nine years of imprisonment, and Su Jinchu was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment. After the sentence was pronounced, the prisoners were ordered to be returned to custody. However, Fan and Su both stated that they did not accept the judgment and would appeal.

In suggesting the above three points as conclusions, it is to prove the fact that products from our country can be promoted for sale in America. Therefore, we should pay serious attention to this fact and take it as a path to develop commerce with America. According to the reporter's opinion, the company should, in accordance with the provisions of Article 4, Section A, of Chapter 1 of its articles of association, initiate the organization of the China Products Standards Company, send personnel to America to promote tea as its primary business, and promote the products that Mr. Zhou deems marketable as its secondary business. This spirit of enthusiasm is highly commendable.
