The sacrificial capital should be raised from those who share Mr. Zhou's aspirations, and the operating capital should be raised from ordinary investors who support the development of foreign trade. This operating capital should be deposited in Shanghai to ensure its safety. In addition, the company should request government approval to issue national goods trial sales bonds to America to purchase the kinds of products that Mr. Zhou considers marketable and try to sell them at the Chicago Exposition to determine the company's secondary business portfolio. Because Mr. Zhou has guaranteed through experience that all products deemed marketable can be sold for profit, the issuance of these bonds is considered to have very little risk. The company's capital is set at US$1 per share, and the bonds are set at RMB 10 per bond to make them easy for the people to purchase. The bond interest rate is set at 1%, to be repaid in five installments on a monthly basis, with each installment repaying 5% of the bond principal. Interest will be paid with the final installment. 50% of the profit from the bond-funded product purchases and operations will be returned to the bondholders, and 50% will be for the benefit and compensation of the China Products Standards Company and this company. In this way, bondholders can be risk-free, and the risk borne by this company seems minimal. Therefore, the above suggestions are made, advocating that this company adopt them in accordance with its aspiration to promote domestic goods and assist production. It is heard that the company's managing director, Wu Zhihao, and general manager, Wu Tingsheng, have expressed their support for this proposal and have instructed the design department to draft an implementation plan for submission to the board of directors and supervisors for discussion.

Forty Chinese Cigarette Factories Petition for a Meeting to Discuss Cigarette Tax Rates 127

Twenty-four Chinese cigarette factories, including the Minzhong Cigarette Company, have repeatedly petitioned the government to revise the tax rates. Since the petitions did not contain concrete proposals, the Minzhong Company, the original proposer, is now putting forward a proposal. The number of factories supporting the revision of tax rates has increased from twenty-four to forty. The text of the petition is transcribed below:

Petition for convening a meeting to publicly discuss cigarette tax rates. It has been found that twenty-four cigarette companies, including Minzhong, jointly petitioned to revise the current cigarette tax rates due to unequal treatment between Chinese and foreign companies, in order to seek relief. The Ministry of Finance's Taxation Department responded with a letter asking the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Association to submit the matter to a general meeting of members for discussion. It was decided to appoint nine review committee members for public review. The review committee then produced a written opinion stating the results and sent it to the association, which forwarded it to the Taxation Department. The original written opinion stated that after the implementation of the two-tier tax system, the annual losses to national tax revenue, cigarette merchants, and tobacco farmers amounted to 44,656,796 yuan, while British-American Tobacco Company enjoyed special privileges worth more than 21,640,000 yuan. These figures were based on accurate data. In theory, there were various reasons why the two-tier tax system could not exist, and the opinion was very thorough. It proposed the organization of a cigarette tax rate review committee, with committee members from the Legislative Yuan, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Industry, Taxation Department, and Chinese Cigarette Factory Association, to hold public discussions in order to determine appropriate and sound tax rates. This would meet the government's financial needs, promote social and economic development, and align with the people's ability to bear the burden, which is extremely fair and easy to implement. However, one month has passed, and the Taxation Department has not taken satisfactory action. The British-American Tobacco Company, taking advantage of this tax increase, continues to enjoy special privileges and drastically reduces cigarette prices, engaging in fierce aggression against Chinese merchants. For example, the price of "Three Cannon Towers" cigarettes has been reduced from 1.1 yuan per tin to 1 yuan. "Caliq" cigarettes have been reduced from 1.7 yuan per tin to 1.6 yuan. "Wuhua" cigarettes have been reduced from 0.5 yuan per tin to 0.4 yuan. The prices of other brands have also been reduced significantly, resulting in a sharp increase in sales and a great loss for Chinese merchants. This further illustrates the importance of tax rates and the severity of foreign oppression. In the past two to three years, the number of Chinese cigarette factories has fallen from 150-160 to 40-50, accounting for two-thirds of the total, all due to unequal tax rates. Learning from past mistakes, unless cigarette tax rates are reformed, Chinese merchants have no hope of survival. Cigarette tax is a pass-through tax. If the tax increase is fair, the increased amount can be passed on to smokers. For example, in this two-tier tax system, the tax increases by 25 yuan per case, which is only 0.5 cents per ten cigarettes. If it can be passed on, smokers will not feel it is too much. If it cannot be passed on, the manufacturers have to bear it. In other words, the increased cigarette tax collected by the government is entirely taken from dozens of Chinese cigarette manufacturers, who will inevitably go bankrupt one after another. Take low-grade cigarettes as an example. The selling price is 120 yuan per case. After deducting the old tax of 55 yuan, the remaining amount is only 65 yuan. Packaging costs at least 30 yuan, leaving only 35 yuan for the business. If the increased tax of 25 yuan cannot be passed on to smokers, the business will only have 10 yuan left. Manufacturers will not be able to manufacture. For those who mainly operate low-grade cigarettes, what other way can they survive besides bankruptcy? In the past two to three years, every time the government increased taxes, many Chinese merchants went bankrupt. The key lies in this. If asked why the tax cannot be passed on, it is because the tax rates set in previous tax increases were unequal, with taxes on low-grade cigarettes increasing while taxes on high-grade cigarettes decreasing. Take this tax increase as an example. The tax on cigarettes with a registered price of 250 yuan or less per case was 55 yuan, which has been changed to 80 yuan for cigarettes with a registered price of 300 yuan or less. That is, the tax on cigarettes priced at 250 yuan or less has increased by 25 yuan, while the tax on cigarettes priced between 250 yuan and 300 yuan has decreased by 15 yuan. When taxes on low-grade cigarettes increase, merchants certainly want to increase prices to pass the burden on to smokers, but high-grade cigarettes enjoy tax relief, so operators of high-grade cigarettes can take advantage of the tax reduction to drastically reduce prices to attract customers. Every time the government revises tax rates, British-American Tobacco Company reduces prices, which is solid proof. At this time, operators of low-grade cigarettes have less resources than those of high-grade cigarettes, but bear a greater tax burden. Therefore, in market competition, if they do not increase prices, the burden will increase sharply, inevitably leading to losses. If they increase prices, high-grade cigarettes will reduce prices to dump their goods, inevitably leading to sluggish sales and rapid spoilage, wiping out capital. Therefore, they are caught in a dilemma. In recent years, all cigarette companies have painfully refrained from increasing prices in order to maintain their original position. Therefore, the result of the tax increase is nothing more than forcing manufacturers to bear the full amount of the new tax increase. In the era of the seven-tier tax system, the tax on each case of low-grade cigarettes was just over 29 yuan. Now it is 80 yuan per case, nearly three times as much, but the market price has not actually increased accordingly, which is clear evidence. From this perspective, the failure to pass on the new tax to smokers is due to the oppression of unequal tax rates. Therefore, to put it bluntly, the increase in unequal tax rates gives high-grade cigarettes a chance to dump their goods, while simultaneously giving low-grade cigarettes a fatal blow. In other words, it gives British-American Tobacco Company a chance to dump their goods and Chinese merchants a fatal blow. In the past two to three years, more than two-thirds of Chinese cigarette merchants have gone bankrupt. Can it be said that this is not caused by poor tax rates? This is from a commercial perspective. The current tax rate must be revised. As for tobacco leaves, the native tobacco leaves produced in Susong, Huanggang, Xinchang, Dengzhou, Guanjun, Guangshui, Junzhou, and other places sold approximately 390,000 bundles annually during the seven-tier tax era before 1930. In January 1930, when the three-tier tax system was introduced, the amount decreased to 265,000 bundles annually. In February 1932, when the two-tier tax system was introduced, the amount further decreased to 115,000 bundles. After the new tax rate was implemented last December, low-grade cigarettes had no sales channels, and these tobacco leaves were ignored. Tobacco farmers have simple minds and have never studied cigarette tax rates. Therefore, although tobacco farmers in Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces have suffered the disaster of rural bankruptcy due to poor cigarette tax rates, they still do not know the reason. Merchants are both the purchasers of native tobacco leaves and the bearers of cigarette taxes, so they know the most. The period of cigarette tax reductions and increases coincides with the period of sluggish sales of local tobacco leaves, echoing each other like shadows following a body. There is a causal relationship, which is obvious to all. If an on-site investigation is conducted in Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces, it can be clearly shown. The original written opinion of the review committee stated that the loss to tobacco farmers after the implementation of the two-tier tax system was 5.15 million yuan per year. This is based on the recent price of tobacco. If calculated based on the seven-tier era in 1930, the average price of local tobacco leaves was 0.2 yuan per pound, and approximately 390,000 bundles were sold annually, each bundle weighing approximately 250 pounds, totaling 96,500,000 pounds, worth a total of 19.3 million yuan. Currently, due to heavy taxes on low-grade cigarettes and sluggish sales, tobacco farmers' annual income of over 19 million yuan has vanished, and they are inevitably doomed. Local porters, boatmen, and native tobacco leaf merchants also become unemployed. Poor tax rates have such a serious impact on the social economy. It is believed that at this time of rural bankruptcy and rampant Red bandits, the government cannot quell the bandits without restoring the rural economy. Without reforming the tax rates that harm China and benefit foreign countries, tobacco farmers will never have hope of recovery. This is from an agricultural perspective. The current tax rate must also be revised. Cigarette tax revenue is approximately 60 million yuan per year, ranking first among inland taxes, and is of great importance to finance. The value of cigarette goods is approximately 120 million yuan per year, making it a major category of imitation machine-made foreign goods, and is of great importance to industry. Native tobacco leaves are an essential agricultural product, and the production area is close to bandit areas, which is also of great importance to the future of bandit suppression. The decision of tax rate is the special privilege of the Legislative Yuan. Therefore, the original written opinion proposed that the Legislative Yuan, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Industry, Taxation Department, and Shanghai Cigarette Factory Association each select several committee members to conduct public discussions, and solemnly stated that meeting the government's financial needs should be the first priority. The opinions also respected the Cigarette Consolidated Tax Regulations announced by the government and adopted the two principles of the seven-tier system according to customs valuation and ad valorem taxation. It is hoped that the Taxation Department will follow the principle of public opinion and handle the matter as soon as possible. However, in the blink of an eye, a month has passed without any approval. The Chinese and foreign merchants can no longer endure the poor tax rates. Therefore, it is requested that the government immediately approve the request made in the written opinion of the Review Committee of the General Meeting of the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Association and conduct public discussions led by the administrative and legislative branches. The main focus should be on complying with the Consolidated Tax Regulations and establishing a strict seven-tier tax system and fair ad valorem tax rates. At this time of commercial war, foreigners are cunning in every way. Only by discussing tax rates in public can the truth be revealed. A fair tax rate that increases tax revenue can be achieved. Not only will our country's industry benefit immensely, but the future of bandit suppression and tax revenue will also see great results. Furthermore, if the government follows Article 5 of the Cigarette Consolidated Tax Regulations, assessing the tax rate of 32.5% according to the customs valuation and dividing it into seven tiers, according to the number of cigarettes sold in Shanghai in February, the tax revenue should be 723,877.875 yuan, which is 79,157.875 yuan more than the current tax rate. The annual increase would be 949,894.500 yuan. Shanghai accounts for just under one-tenth of the national tax revenue. Therefore, if the ten-tier tax system is implemented nationwide, the annual increase in tax revenue would be over 9 million yuan. Five types of forms are prepared separately: (A) Statistical Table of Cigarette Sales and Tax Revenue in Shanghai in February, (B) Table of the Number of Cases of Cigarettes Sold in Shanghai in February Reassessed Based on the Assumed Seven-Tier Tax Rate, (C) Comparison Table of the Assumed Seven-Tier Tax Rate and the Current Two-Tier Tax Rate, (D) Table of the Percentage of the Assumed Seven-Tier Tax Rate and the Current Two-Tier Tax Rate for the Total Cigarette Sales in Shanghai in March, (E) Comparison Table of the Budgeted National Tax Revenue Based on the Assumed Seven-Tier Tax Rate and the Current Two-Tier Tax Rate. Each table is accompanied by an explanation to prove that the seven-tier tax system is beneficial to the government's tax revenue and Chinese merchants' business. On the contrary, the two-tier tax system only benefits British-American Tobacco Company and is detrimental to the government and Chinese merchants. What to choose? The government should investigate further and it will be easy to see the truth. This petition is submitted to the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Control Yuan, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Industry, Military Affairs Commission, and Taxation Department by the following petitioners: Minzhong Cigarette Company, Fuxin Cigarette Company, Huaxing Cigarette Company, Datong Cigarette Company, Meixing Mingji, Huamei Tobacco Company, Zhonghe Tobacco Company, Huabi Tobacco Company, Fuchang Cigarette Company, Hexing Tobacco Company, Daxing Cigarette Company, Huafu Cigarette Factory, Zhongyuan Cigarette Company, Donghai Cigarette Factory, Zhida Xinji Cigarette Company, Huaping Cigarette Company, Shanghai China Taiping Cigarette Company, Youlibaoji Cigarette Factory, Dada Cigarette Factory, Jiangzhe Cigarette Company, Xinhua Cigarette Company, Dachina Cigarette Company, Shanghai Cigarette Company, Jinshatai Ji Tobacco Company, Yuanli Cigarette Company, Fuxing Cigarette Shop, Jiuyigongji Tobacco Company, Changming Tobacco Company, Yonghe Cigarette Company, Huaxin Cigarette Factory, Xinmin Cigarette Company, Jinshan Cigarette Factory, Yicheng Company, Delong Cigarette Factory, Dahua Zhongji Cigarette Company, Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company.

However, the association should send personnel to supervise the issuance of licenses to avoid disputes. (4) Proposal to ban jai alai and dog racing venues. It was reported that the district branches of the Citizens' Association had sent letters requesting a strict ban. Resolved: Huang Xianggu, Mao Yun, Shang Mujiang, Cheng Zhusun, and Tong Lizhang were appointed as five committee members to draft an official letter for submission to the French authorities requesting a ban. The appointed committee members include Cheng Zhusun, Shang Mujiang, Qu Zhenhua, Gu Wensheng, Wu Xiu, Mao Yun, Zhu Wenqi, Huang Xianggu, Tong Lizhang, and others, totaling nine people, with Cheng Zhusun as the convener. (6) A letter was received from the ten district branches of the Citizens' Association regarding the Xu Jia Hui French Police's infringement of police powers. Resolved: Tang Jingxi was appointed to investigate and then negotiate. (7) A letter was received from the Repair and Sales Bicycle Trade Association regarding the French Municipal Council's increase in taxes. Resolved: The association should wait for the trade association to provide detailed reasons before handling the matter. After the above proposals were discussed and just as the meeting was about to adjourn, a letter was suddenly received from the Shanghai Federation of Machine-Made National Goods Factories, reporting that the French Municipal Council was collecting an annual inspection fee of 70 yuan for the boiler inspection of the Hongxing Socks Factory. Since the issue of factory inspection sovereignty has not been resolved, it is difficult to recognize it and a request for dealing with the matter and negotiation was received. The association immediately forwarded the original letter to the Chairman for handling.

Letter from the Shanghai Federation of Machine-Made National Goods Factories. Yesterday, the Shanghai Federation of Machine-Made National Goods Factories sent a letter to the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association to strongly protest the French Municipal Council's collection of inspection fees from the Hongxing Socks Factory. The original text reads: "Respected Sirs, we have recently received a letter from our member, Hongxing Socks Factory, stating that on the 6th of this month, personnel from the Health Bureau of the Concession, accompanied by the Fire Brigade, brought equipment to inspect our factory's boiler and injected 126 pounds of cold pressure. As a result, they deemed it satisfactory and left. Unexpectedly, we received a notice today stating that our factory should pay an annual inspection fee and other fees, totaling 70 yuan, which is deeply shocking. We believe that this is an entirely new initiative for factories, and our factory cannot rashly set a precedent, etc.," and a photograph of the French notice is attached. We have learned that the issue of factory inspection rights has been disputed between the Chinese and foreign authorities for a long time. Last year, the Public Concession authorities ordered Yiyuan Rubber Factory, etc., to improve and relocate, ostensibly to prevent public danger, but in reality, to seize inspection rights. Now, the French Concession authorities send personnel to inspect factories without prior written notice to the factory, relying only on a business card. If unscrupulous individuals take the opportunity to commit fraud against factories, the French authorities cannot escape responsibility. Furthermore, the collection of inspection fees concerns our country's sovereignty. Before the issue of inspection rights is resolved, there is no basis for discussing this. We have always admired your association as the highest Chinese authority in the French Concession, cherishing national rights and being consistent. We hereby send this letter in preparation, and hope that you will investigate and strongly protest to prevent coveting and guard against pretexts, which is our earnest expectation. Respectfully addressed to the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association."

The National Match Industry Held its First Representative Conference Yesterday, and Drafted the National Match Control Outline, etc. 130

The China National Match Industry Federation held its first temporary representative conference at its office on Sichuan Road at 5:00 PM yesterday to discuss important matters such as the Match Control Outline and the election of seven match control committee members. Those in attendance included Liu Hongsheng representing the Shanghai Dachina Factory, Gao Songfu representing the Shanghai Dachina Factory, Zhang Xinwu representing the Tianjin Danhua Factory, Zhao Xuanqing representing the Hangzhou Guanghua Factory, Xiang Jiyun representing the Beijing Danhua Factory, Qu Jiantang representing the Qingdao Xingye Factory, Wang Ruizan representing the Tianjin Beiyang Factory, Cong Dezi representing the Jinan Zhenye Factory, and approximately 30 other people. Liu Hongsheng, the chairman, delivered the opening speech. The representatives discussed the Match Control Outline and the method of electing the control committee members. The meeting adjourned at approximately 9:00 PM. It is reported that the meeting will continue this morning. The following is an excerpt from the National Match Control Outline and the Joint Business Outline drafted by the federation:

Control Outline (A) National Match Control Outline: (1) Petition the government to establish a National Match Control Committee, with seven members from the match industry to be elected by the industry; (2) The powers of the committee are as follows: (1) To stipulate the production and sales volume of each factory; (2) To review and approve the value and selling price of each brand of matches; (3) To restrict the establishment of new factories; (4) To unify the accounting system; (5) To improve technology; (6) To adjudicate various disputes between match industry members; (3) The production quota is based on the average production volume of each factory recorded by the government from the implementation of the consolidated tax to December 4, 1933 (statistics on the consolidated tax are available for Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Shandong, Henan, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Hebei, Shanxi, Chahar, and Suiyuan provinces, which can be used as a basis. Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian will be investigated separately. The implementation in Shaanxi, Gansu, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan provinces, where the consolidated tax has not been implemented, will be temporarily postponed); (If factories have merged, the stipulated production quota will not be lost due to the merger); (Matches sold abroad are not subject to the quota restriction, but must be approved by the committee in advance); (4) Restricting the establishment of factories is limited to the factories currently established, and is effective for both Chinese and foreign factories. Factories that have already been established but have not yet shipped goods must be approved by the committee before they can start production; (5) Dispatch personnel to factories to monitor production. If the quota is exceeded, the excess matches will be sealed separately and returned when the factory's production is insufficient in the future; (6) Petition the government to designate potassium chlorate as a special product for match manufacturing, and the passport shall only be issued by the Match Control Committee; (7) The transportation and sales of matches shall be handled by the joint business contract organized by each factory, but with the approval of the committee, the committee can petition the government to suspend its production and sales rights.

Joint Business (B) Match Joint Business Outline: (1) Divide the country into several regions, establish a joint business office in Shanghai as the headquarters, and establish branches or sub-branches in suitable locations in other regions, completely managed by merchants; (2) Dispatch personnel to factories to manage the receipt and delivery of finished products in the factory or outside the warehouse, and report on other matters; (3) The joint business headquarters or branch is organized by each factory by contributing capital and signing a contract; (4) Each factory may elect a fully authorized representative to form a committee to supervise the distribution of sales by the joint business office; (5) The products of each factory are distributed and sold by the joint headquarters, branch, or sub-branch. The shipping manifest is signed by the joint office and delivered to the customer to pick up the goods from the on-site manager. The price obtained from the sale, the wholesale price, is paid to each factory monthly according to the actual sales volume. The surplus, after deducting expenses and public bonds, is distributed monthly. If there are losses, they are also recognized monthly; (6) The payment of the business office's capital, the distribution of sales, the distribution of surplus, and the burden of losses are all based on the standard stipulated in Article 3 of the Control Outline.

Employee of the China Industrial Bank Embezzles Huge Sums of Depositors' Money, Reaching a Staggering 18,000 Yuan 139

Zhou Xiong, a 24-year-old Cantonese man working in the savings department of the China Industrial Bank at 1300 North Sichuan Road, residing at 130 Tangjiawan Road, French Concession, was introduced to the bank in 1928 by a Mr. Luo. He opened a "Huili Cosmetics Store" on Nanjing Road. Recently, his business failed, resulting in significant losses. In addition, his household income was not enough to cover his expenses. Therefore, from 1931 to January of this year, he embezzled 18,000 yuan in silver dollars in succession for his own use and then abandoned his job and fled without a trace. After the bank manager discovered this, he negotiated with the guarantor. Later, Zhou sent a letter to the bank, enclosing two warehouse receipts for 22 boxes of cosmetics worth several thousand gold pieces as temporary collateral. He said he would find a way to settle the rest. The other day, Zhou suddenly arrived at the bank, intending to resume his job, but the Hongkou Police Station was notified. Chinese Detective Zhu Jihuang took a warrant from the court and rushed to arrest him, taking him to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the Municipal Council stated the circumstances and said that the 22 boxes of cosmetics had been deposited in the China Industrial Bank warehouse on North Suzhou Road. Now, the police station is prosecuting him for breach of trust and other crimes under Article 366 of the Criminal Law. The way he embezzled the silver dollars was to increase the amounts withdrawn by customers from the savings department, such as adding 500 or 1,000 yuan to a 1,000 yuan withdrawal, etc., without a fixed amount. The bank is still investigating the accounts of the depositors handled by the defendant. He confessed to everything at the police station and requested a postponement. The letter and two warehouse receipts for the cosmetics were presented for inspection. Judge Wu Zehan questioned the defendant and ordered him to be remanded in custody and the hearing rescheduled.

Mr. Tang Weizhi's Seventieth Birthday; Students Raise Funds to Build the Rujing Memorial Hall 142

Mr. Tang Weizhi served as the president of Nanyang University for fifteen years, with remarkable achievements. After resigning in 1920, he founded the National Studies Academy in Wuxi, personally teaching classes every day, tireless even in his old age. To celebrate Mr. Tang's 70th birthday this year, former and current students have agreed to raise funds to build the Rujing Hall on the shores of Taihu Lake in Wuxi, to be a permanent memorial. The construction cost is set at a minimum of 10,000 yuan. A preparatory committee has been established, donation notices have been printed and sent out to solicit donations. The deadline is set for the end of April.

Taxpaying Chinese Residents Repeatedly Have Their Telephone Lines Cut Off by the Telephone Company Without Reason; Shen Yiqian Requests Compensation for Line Cut-Off Losses; Qian Longzhang Does Not Accept the Company's Apology 144

The Shanghai Concession Taxpaying Chinese Residents Association sent letters to the Public Concession Municipal Council and replied to Mr. Qian Longzhang regarding the telephone company cutting off users' telephone lines without reason. The letters are recorded separately below.

Lawyer Shen Yiqian 145

Dear Sir, According to a letter from taxpayer Shen Yiqian, the taxpayer's home telephone number is 31458. On the morning of March 29th at 9:30, the Shanghai Telephone Company suddenly cut off the line, rendering it unusable. When inquiring at number 01, the reply was that the machine was damaged and someone was sent to repair it. When calling the company again in the afternoon, it was said that the line was cut off because the fee had not been paid. The taxpayer immediately sent a letter to the general manager of the company, but there has been no reply to date. However, the taxpayer's telephone bill (from February 1st to April 30th of this year) was paid in full at 8:50 am on March 29th, as evidenced by the receipt. The telephone was still working at 9:10 after the fee was paid. To cut off the telephone line after paying the fee, and without prior notice before the cut-off, is unacceptable. The taxpayer is a lawyer, and the business losses are very significant. It is requested that your association send a letter to the Municipal Council, which manages and supervises the franchised business, to immediately order the company to restore the line and compensate for all losses. The receipt has been sent to the association. Please investigate and handle it together with the letters from our association on March 29th and April 5th.

Physician Qian Longzhang 146

Dear Sir, According to a letter from taxpayer Physician Qian Longzhang, "The taxpayer's telephone number is 32345. The Shanghai Telephone Company stopped the call without reason. I have written a letter requesting your association to forward it to the management and supervision authority, requesting that it be ordered to restore the call and compensate for the damage. Now, the telephone company restored the call at 9:00 am the next morning after being notified by the company's telephone. So, from the time it was stopped to the time it was restored, it was a total of 24 hours. I have received a letter from the Shanghai Telephone Company on April 4th, saying that it apologizes for any inconvenience caused to the taxpayer due to the erroneous disconnection. I think that the responsibility of the company is to make it convenient for the public. If it makes it inconvenient for people, and it can only apologize to private individuals, it is too trivial to supervise the management agency. The taxpayer will not give up the request for compensation for damages unless the company officially sends a letter of apology to the Municipal Council and your association." This situation has come to the association. Our association believes that Dr. Qian's attitude is very reasonable. Otherwise, it is not enough to see that the Shanghai Telephone Company has a supervisory and management agency above it.

The Taxpayer Association replied directly: We received your letter of April 11th, regarding not directly accepting the Shanghai Telephone Company's apology for the unjustified line cut-off. We have noted everything. Our association believes that this attitude is very correct and has forwarded the letter to the Public Concession Municipal Council. This is a reply to Physician Qian Longzhang.

The Railway Bureau Extends the Validity Date of Discount Tickets to Seven Days for Both the Railway and Intermodal Transportation 149

The Traffic Department of the Railway Bureau issued a circular to all stations yesterday regarding the extension of the validity date of discount tickets for round trips. The circular stated, "The validity date of the outbound journey of intermodal transportation discount tickets has been limited to three days from the date of issuance. It has been found that employees at various stations often do not have enough time to use these tickets within the validity period when applying for them, and repeated requests have been made to extend the period, which is reasonable. From now on, all discount tickets, whether for the railway or intermodal transportation, will be changed to a validity date of seven days, in line with the domestic intermodal transportation discount tickets. The validity period for the return journey will still be handled according to the previous regulations. In addition, if employees or their family members request to add a 'permitted to ride on special express train' stamp due to time constraints, it should be allowed, except for the Shanghai-Ping express train, to add this stamp and ride on other special express trains of the railway. In addition to reporting to the railway and distributing it to the sub-bureaus, please comply."

Municipal Fisheries Guidance Institute Releases the Production and Sales of Aquatic Products, Greatly Affected by the Dumping of Japanese Fish 151

According to the Central News Agency, according to the Shanghai Municipal Fisheries Guidance Institute, the total quantity of various aquatic products produced and sold in the city in March this year was 45,006 dan and 79 jin, with a total value of 735,907.69 yuan. Compared with the previous month, the quantity decreased by 489 dan and 35 jin, while the value increased by 54,633.25 yuan. This is because the various imported seafood products this month were mostly valuable dried products, so the quantity was small but the value was high. Secondly, after the end of the Lunar New Year, the demand for freshwater fish and other products was high, so the value was also higher. As for the city's fishing vessels, although the catch increased, the value decreased. This is due to the impact of the dumping of Japanese fish in the market. The quantity and value of other ice-fresh fish boats, ice-fresh barrels, and various salted fish decreased compared with the previous month. The quantity and value of frozen fish and canned aquatic products both increased slightly.

The Municipal Health Bureau Adds Nine New Hospital Wards; Two to Begin Construction Within Days, Completing in Three Months; The Rest to be Built Sequentially, Completed Within Two Years 158

Since Director Li Ting'an took office at the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, he has been determined to rectify the situation, and a new atmosphere prevails. Although after the ravages of war, everything is being rebuilt, and his achievements are remarkable. The Contagious Disease Hospital, recently established on Tongji Road in Zhabei, is perfectly equipped, has excellent doctors, and treats patients with exceptional care. Residents in the vicinity who are infected with epidemics all go there for treatment. Since its opening, only a month ago, the number of people seeking treatment has reached as high as 479. The current 62 beds are far from sufficient. Director Li, in view of this, despite extreme financial difficulties, has saved expenses in every possible way, and raised funds to plan to add nine new hospital wards in the shortest possible time. Two of these can begin construction within days, with a capacity of 50 beds, and are expected to be completed in about three months. In addition, construction will continue sequentially, and it is estimated that they will be completed within two years. These nine hospital wards will all be built according to the latest international designs for contagious disease wards. Once all are completed, the hospital plans to separately house several types of legally defined infectious diseases, limiting each ward to one disease, so that the work of isolation can be fully achieved, and the danger of infection can be avoided. The benefits to sick people will be considerable. However, in recent days, many hospitalized patients have been impatient with their stay. As soon as their condition improves slightly, they request to leave the hospital. Their thinking is still very outdated. This is all due to the failure to popularize education, and the lack of intellectual enlightenment. It is hoped that the education authorities will pay attention to this.

Yu Shicheng's Lawsuit Against the Jing'an Vessel is Moved to Shanghai for Trial 160

Yu Shicheng, the owner of the Fuzhou small steamboat, filed a lawsuit with the Zhenjiang Court due to the sinking of his boat after being struck in Jiangyin. He requested the detention of the Sanbei's Jing'an vessel as an emergency measure. Based on Yu's complaint, the Zhenjiang Court, upon the Jing'an's arrival in Zhenjiang, attempted to seize the vessel without summoning the shipowner for questioning. When shipowner Liu urgently telegraphed the Shanghai Bureau to report this, the Sanbei General Company telegraphed the Zhenjiang Court to inquire who would guarantee the huge losses incurred by the ship detention if the lawsuit was unfounded. After this telegram, the Zhenjiang Court released the ship back to Shanghai. Sanbei has now suspended sailing on the one hand and investigated and learned that the original plaintiff, Yu Shicheng, also resides in Shanghai, and the Jing'an vessel has now arrived in Shanghai for berthing. The shipowner and crew are all in Shanghai awaiting the legal proceedings. Therefore, they requested the Zhenjiang Court to transfer this false accusation case to the Shanghai Special District Court. Yesterday afternoon, a letter arrived from Zhenjiang stating that the Zhenjiang Court had granted the Sanbei Company's request, and that the case of whether the Jing'an vessel had sunk the Fuzhou small steamboat would be transferred to the Shanghai Special District Court for trial. The entire case file will be transferred to Shanghai and handed over to the Special District Court, awaiting a scheduled hearing.

Zhang Zhiyun's Self-Accusation is Approved for Withdrawal 161

Zhang Zhiyun, who was formerly selected as a movie queen, filed a self-accusation against Zhou Xiaobo for violating the cohabitation agreement and endangering public morals. The First Special District Court repeatedly summoned her for questioning, but Zhang never appeared in court. On the one hand, she submitted a statement to the court denying the lawsuit against Zhou, and on the other hand, she made other expressions to her attorney, Dan Yuhua, changing her attitude frequently, which drew the judge's attention. Therefore, at the last hearing, Magistrate Liu specifically instructed Attorney Dan that if she evaded the summons again, she would be detained according to the law and transferred to the Procuratorate. Yesterday afternoon, the date for the hearing arrived again, but Zhang was still not seen. Attorney Dan then submitted a written statement, stating that this statement was personally written by the plaintiff, Zhang Zhiyun, in which she confessed to all her previous improprieties, requested leniency and exemption from investigation, and stated that the case had indeed been settled out of court, and requested that the self-accusation be approved for withdrawal. After examining the statement, Magistrate Liu determined that it was indeed Zhang's writing. Since she voluntarily wanted to settle the dispute, the withdrawal should be approved, and ruled that the case would not be accepted. The Zhang-Zhou dispute has thus been resolved.

Reading Questions and Answers

How to Study Education 175

— Reply from 丨丨 to Wang Yin 丨丨

Mr. Wang Yin wrote, inquiring about the ways to study education and what fundamental knowledge is necessary for studying education. We hereby present our opinions in response as follows:

Before entering the main text, let us first ask Mr. Wang Yin, what is the purpose you hold in studying education?

Perhaps Mr. Wang Yin will think that we are asking too foolishly. A person has a purpose for doing anything, unless that person is a fool who sows blindly. Yes, we believe Mr. Wang Yin has a purpose, but the problem lies here. If A has a certain purpose for doing the same thing, and B has another purpose, then their achievements and results will inevitably be different accordingly. For example, consider manufacturing poisonous gas. Some manufacture it for the needs of the chemical industry, and some manufacture it to supply the needs of war. The former is beneficial to human society, while the latter is a poison that destroys human society. In doing things, we should not only have a purpose, but also have a proper purpose. If the starting point is wrong, then the entire course of your undertaking will fall into error.

Regarding this question, we can cite some of the most common opinions in the minds of general education researchers to answer.

First, there are those who advocate saving the nation through education. They elevate education to the highest level, believing that education is omnipotent; that education can restore "morality and public sentiment," and that education can save "the dying." When they see that their industry is not as developed as other countries, and that their guns are not as sharp as other countries, they think it is the result of education, so they engage in some kind of military education. When they see the people on the verge of starvation and the whole country in a state of panic, they also think it is the result of education, so they engage in some kind of vocational education, production education. May I ask, is this possible? Can education save a country from decline? Facts have already given us a clear answer: in the past twenty years, Chinese education has had very little effect on the people and the country. Those who study education with this purpose, if they are not intentionally deceiving themselves, willingly helping those with ulterior motives to deceive and anesthetize the people, will inevitably fall into despair and never find a way out.

Secondly, there are those who advocate the purity of education. They believe that education transcends society and is a pure and noble undertaking unpolluted by the secular world. On the one hand, they pride themselves, stubbornly adhering to the prejudice that "all occupations are inferior, only studying is noble." On the other hand, they isolate themselves from society. That is, let the warlords engage in melee, let the bureaucrats be corrupt, education is not affected. May I ask, is this possible? The movement for independent education funding, which has been advocated for more than ten years, still only results in the habit of appropriating education funds for military expenditures. If we are not blind, we will never fail to see these facts. If you must proclaim yourself pure, then unless you are willing to starve to death. It can be seen that education researchers who take this path also have no way out.

So, what is the proper purpose of studying education? A purpose is not determined by one person's imagination, but rather, on the one hand, should be based on the actual needs of society, and on the other hand, should recognize what role the knowledge we study plays in society.

The evolution of education is determined by a certain social productivity and relations of production. Primitive education is inseparable from human life, that is, mental labor is combined with physical labor. With the development of productivity, there was a division of labor in society, and then classes were born. Thus, mental labor and physical labor were split, and education was no longer owned by laborers, but became the exclusive privilege of a privileged class, serving as one of the tools for ruling the people. Under the feudal social system, the rulers were afraid that the people would rise up in rebellion because of hunger, so they promoted the education of "loyalty, filial piety, integrity, and righteousness." "Starving to death does not matter, only fear of lacking integrity and not being able to be loyal to the master," this is their main task of education. In capitalist society, because capital production organization requires organized laborers, industrial officers at all levels, there is a capitalist class education system. The task of capitalist education, on the one hand, is nothing more than continuously creating production personnel for the production organization to maintain the production process. On the other hand, in order to expand the market and occupy the market, it attempts to create thousands upon thousands of capital soldiers. This is the essence of so-called military education and patriotic education; as for production education, it is only focused on improving labor intensity, increasing labor productivity, and expanding the exploitation process. In fact, in the late stage of capitalism, as a result of the rationalization of production, the division of labor becomes more detailed, and laborers do not need specialized knowledge, so workers' education is no longer decided by capitalists. Education in modern society is no longer for the people, and it is inevitably the exclusive property of a few people. The so-called public education is just empty talk (to be continued).

Page 17

Bank of China Business Report, Republic of China, Year 22

Introduction 176

The national economy of the 22nd year of the Republic of China. In a nutshell, it is simply the obvious manifestation of the pathological state of the 21st year! In a part of North China, the counties on the border of Hebei and Chahar suffered slightly from war. The Yellow River area of Shandong suffered slightly from floods. Other areas had no major accidents. Politics gradually became stable, and the field harvest was also abundant. However, the general price of agricultural products fell, land depreciated, and farmers became increasingly impoverished. Fortunately, the price of cotton did not fall as severely as other agricultural products; therefore, the rural conditions of the provinces of Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Shaanxi, and Henan were slightly better than those of other provinces. In the central Yangtze River region, Sichuan and Jiangxi were ravaged by communist bandits. Hunan, Anhui, and Jiangsu suffered from the sharp drop in rice prices and the decline of silk and tea. Farmers'

income decreased even more. In a part of South China, remittances from overseas Chinese continued to decline, and rice was supplied from abroad. The society was economically impoverished, even more so than the Yangtze River provinces. Considering China as a whole, the huge loss of Manchurian export trade led to a daily increase in the number of excess imports, and the outflow of raw gold and silver was even greater. Furthermore, the low price of agricultural products caused the people's purchasing power to decrease more and more, and the sales of domestic industrial products became increasingly diminished. This is a phenomenon that should occur during pathological changes, an inevitable result. However, what should be noted is that the pathological state of the 22nd year was mostly due to the repercussions of the global recession. However, like a weak body neglecting hygiene, it is easier for external pathogens to invade. Considering that things become more urgent in times of desperation, the pathological state of the 22nd year was already known in the 21st year. It was only in the 22nd year that the urgency of implementation was realized. During this year, the entire country, from top to bottom, knew that improving the countryside could not be delayed. Furthermore, they knew that improving the countryside, in a negative sense, required removing obstacles and reducing burdens; in a positive sense, it required various economic constructions to proceed simultaneously. Therefore, the central government issued a general order to eliminate all exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies, and improved railway transportation, reduced transportation costs, and increased the construction of highways and railways. It also implemented cotton industry control and promoted cooperative movements. All these measures were aimed at rescuing the countryside and indirectly benefiting from it. Although large-scale plans have not yet been seen, the government, compelled by its own self-interest, gradually realized the importance of cultivating the people's strength. Therefore, who knows if the pain of rural bankruptcy today will not be the price of rural revitalization in the future? This is the image of the turn of fortune amidst the profound and painful experiences of the 22nd year, which is filled with substance and brilliance, and depends on the rising up of the national people!

Bank of China's Operations for the Twenty-Second Year of the Republic (1933) 177

The bank's operations in the twenty-second year followed the direction announced in last year's report: reducing deposit interest rates to prevent unnatural credit expansion; lowering loan interest rates to ease the burden on industry and commerce; establishing inland branches to encourage the flow of capital inland; and increasing warehouse facilities to promote the circulation of goods and supplement rural finance. Although the implementation fell short of the desired 20-30%, fortunately, due to the bank's deep relationship with society, these measures have received considerable feedback. This year, inland lending rates gradually decreased, with some reductions of 2-3% compared to previous years. The increasing number of inland financial institutions and the competitive advancement of various rural loan programs are in no small part due to the bank's influence, which is not only fortunate for the general financial sector, but also gratifying to the bank's shareholders. However, despite reduced deposit rates, deposits did not decrease; despite lower lending rates, merchants in various regions were exhausted and lacked good credit; and the prices of various agricultural products plummeted. Even with goods as collateral, there were concerns about stagnation and losses at any time. Therefore, the rate of increase in lending could not match the increase in deposits, and the bank's profits were gradually diminishing. This is an inevitable fact in the face of the general trend of economic downturn, which should be understood by our shareholders. As for the establishment of inland branches and warehouses, it is not possible to achieve these goals in one fell swoop, as it requires cultivating talent suitable for inland areas and planning appropriate facilities. Therefore, gradual progress is necessary. Regarding banking operations, the difficulties faced by branches in the south were greater than those in the north. In Sichuan province, the communists suddenly rose up, and in Jiangxi province, the communists had not yet been completely suppressed. Coupled with the Fujian Incident, all industries were temporarily stagnant, and money houses in Fujian and Guangdong provinces closed down one after another, causing financial chaos. Fortunately, the local branches acted cautiously and did not suffer significant losses. At the same time, they spared no effort to support the market to prevent the collapse of the local financial foundations. However, at a time when the government's laissez-faire economic policy is failing and the old-fashioned commercial and financial organizations are being eliminated, the difficulties faced by the bank in its position are self-evident. The only option is to uphold the bank's long-held principle of prudence, strive to increase efficiency and reduce costs for ourselves to consolidate the existing foundation, and continue the current policy for society, guiding the financial sector onto a healthy track!

(A) Business Overview

(1) Deposits

A. Total Deposits The total outstanding balance of various deposits in the twenty-second year was 539,284,527.16, an increase of 62,736,473.73 compared to the twenty-first year. Analyzing the comparison: (1) The outstanding balance of current deposits was 189,769,090.68, an increase of 6,168,033.09 compared to the twenty-first year; (2) The outstanding balance of fixed deposits was 211,200,849.23, a decrease of 23,431,198.36 compared to the twenty-first year; this is because 56,884,670.47, the amount of guarantee reserve for issuance, was transferred out this year (see the section on the composition of the preparation for the issuance of banknotes below). If added to the calculation, it would be an increase of 33,453,472.11 compared to the twenty-first year; (3) The outstanding balance of interbank deposits was 138,314,587.25, an increase of 79,999,639.00 compared to the twenty-first year.

B. Number of Depositors The number of depositors in the twenty-second year was 136,729, an increase of 22,236 compared to the twenty-first year. If the number of 76,127 in the nineteenth year is taken as the base number, the index of the number of depositors increasing year by year can be calculated as follows:

This is the result of the inability of imports and exports to offset each other, and it is a sign of the depletion of capital in the interior.

(4) Foreign Exchange

The bank's foreign exchange business has always been compiled first according to US dollars and then converted into national currency at the current price for the convenience of calculation. If calculated in gold coins this year, the foreign exchange business has made considerable progress compared to the twenty-first year. However, due to the drop in the exchange rate of the US dollar, the number converted into national currency is smaller than last year, except for remittances and term bills.

(5) Revision of the Preparation Subject of Issuance of Exchange Notes and Loan and Loan Comparison Table

At the end of the twenty-second year, the total amount of exchange notes in circulation at the bank was 183,726,997.37, a decrease of 700,000 yuan compared to the total amount in circulation at the end of the twenty-first year. In terms of the reserve fund for exchange notes, the cash reserve was 115,863,202.90, accounting for 63% of the total amount in circulation; the guarantee reserve was 67,863,794.47, accounting for 37% of the total amount in circulation. According to the bank's previous externally published loan comparison table, the cash guarantee and the preparation submitted by the note-receiving firms were listed together as a whole preparation amount for the total amount in circulation. In addition to the cash and guarantee preparation of more than 60% of the firms, all of the bank's guarantee preparation was actually made up of valuable securities and real estate deeds, which have always been internally demarcated, recorded in separate accounts, and stored in separate warehouses. However, in the loan comparison table, this asset used as guarantee preparation was still included in the operating asset subject, and had not been separated. It was only listed again in the deposit item on the liability side to clarify the preparation and to seek a balance of assets and liabilities. With this method, there are shortcomings of repeated expression on the asset side, and there are many virtual transfer numbers on the asset side. This year, the past methods were revised, and all valuable securities of 49,828,199.70 and operating real estate of 7,056,470.77, which were used to fill the bank's guarantee preparation, are no longer listed separately under the operating asset and liability subject in the loan comparison table, so that the various asset and liability numbers published by the bank become more precise.

(6) Valuable Securities

At the end of the twenty-second year, the total amount of valuable securities at the bank was 81,847,045.91 (the guarantee preparation part was 49,828,199.70, and the operating part was 32,018,846.21), accounting for 8.9% of the total assets, an increase of 17,302,599.70 compared to 64,544,446.21 in the twenty-first year. Because fixed deposits have increased sharply, the increase is as above for the sake of decentralized use. At the same time, because the market price of British and American gold has fallen sharply in the twenty-second year, the gold bond component has been lowered to maintain the stability of property value.
