(7) Profit and Loss

A. Various Expenses The various expenses in the twenty-second year were more than 6,053,000 yuan, a decrease of more than 12,000 yuan compared to the twenty-first year. In the twenty-second year, the total volume of the bank's business increased compared to the previous year, but the total amount of expenses was still able to maintain the original state, which is the result of the bank's efforts to save money in the past year. It is hoped that the establishment of more institutions and the increase in business will continue to maintain the status quo in terms of expenses.

B. Profit Distribution The net profit in the twenty-second year was 1,923,975.14. After deducting one-tenth of the amount, which is 192,397.51, as public reserve fund according to the regulations, the remaining 1,731,577.63, plus the balance brought forward from the previous year of 4,816.65, less the 7% interest on official and commercial shares of 1,729,854.00, the remaining 6,540.28 is still listed under the profit carry-over item.

(B) Business Operations

In recent years, the circulation of funds in national urban ports has been slow, and it has been extremely difficult to find investment channels. It is even more difficult to consider both obtaining security from the bank's standpoint during the use of funds, and at the same time paying attention to assisting domestic production and alleviating economic panic. The bank's business operations this year have the following noteworthy aspects:

(1) Industrial Loans In the twenty-second year, domestic factories were affected by the decline of rural areas and the dumping of foreign goods, and there were frequent reports of closures and reduced work. Fortunately, the general industry is striving for survival, and its own has made considerable progress. The bank adheres to its long-standing policy of deep cooperation with the industrial sector and strives to assist. This year, the total amount of industrial loans reached 42,455,468 yuan, an increase of 4,020,045 yuan, or more than 10%, compared to last year; an increase of 11,247,814 yuan, or 36%, compared to the previous year. The components of various industries are as follows:

(1) Cotton Mills 56.35

(2) Flour Mills 12.49

(3) Silk Mills 9.31

(4) Oil Mills 4.23

(5) Dyeing and Weaving Mills 3.48

(6) Egg Factories 2.78

(7) Food Factories 1.99

(8) Daily Necessities Factories 1.67

(9) Paper and Printing Factories 1.45

(10) Chemical Industry Factories 1.14

(11) Building Materials Factories 0.95

(12) Handicrafts 0.84

(13) Iron and Electrical Machinery Factories 0.71

(14) Rubber Factories 0.50

(15) Woolen Factories 0.45

(16) Tobacco Factories 0.40

(17) Other 1.26

Among the industrial loans mentioned in the above table, the yarn industry is the largest. Fortunately, the yarn factories assisted by the bank have been able to improve their work and revitalize their survival even in the midst of storms. In the future, it is planned to urge them to improve in terms of technology and management, and to cooperate with them in spirit in addition to economic strength, so that both the bank and the industry can benefit. (2) Agricultural Loans

(A) Agricultural Product Loans This year, we will use the bank's existing warehouse facilities in more than 80 locations to the greatest extent possible to mortgage agricultural products to seek the initial relief of stabilizing prices. At the end of the twenty-second year, agricultural product mortgages such as cotton, cocoons, rice, grains, tobacco, tea, etc. totaled more than 19.5 million yuan; cotton accounted for the largest proportion, with more than 8.19 million yuan; North China accounted for 70% of the morning, and the Yangtze River Basin accounted for 30%. The amount of cotton mortgaged is valued at approximately 11 million yuan. At the end of the twenty-second year, the market and factories had approximately 1.2 million dan of cotton in stock, valued at more than 50 million yuan, and the bank's mortgage component accounted for approximately one-fifth.

(B) Small Loans to Farmers In the second half of this year, 15 agricultural product warehouses were established in agricultural product distribution centers in various regions to promote small loans to farmers. The amount of the loan is not fixed, and some are only one yuan and a few corners. The interest is extremely low, not exceeding one point. At the end of this year, the approved loan quota was 1,012,600 yuan, and the actual loan was more than 622,000 yuan, with 14,597 households. (C) Cooperative Loans The bank will provide loans to cooperative societies that have been effectively managed to assist them. The most important ones are the Zouping Rural Improvement Association, the Dingxian Civilian Promotion Association, and the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee.

(3) Establishment of More Inland Institutions In order to seek the inward flow of capital, more institutions must be established in the interior. This year, 40 branches were added in locations with relatively stable local order, convenient transportation, and centers for the distribution of goods: 13 in Jiangsu Province, 4 in Zhejiang Province, 4 in Anhui Province, 1 in Hunan Province, 5 in Sichuan Province, 1 in Hebei Province, 4 in Henan Province, 2 in Shaanxi Province, 4 in Shandong Province, and 2 in Shanxi Province; 2 in Shanghai, 1 in Tianjin, and 1 in Shenyang, for a total of 44 additional institutions. Together with the old institutions, there are a total of 181 institutions. (4) Increase in Inland Lending and Reduction in Interest Rates Of the 28 million yuan of additional loans issued this year, only 35% of the loans were issued in ports, and approximately 65% of the loans were issued in the interior. As for the interest rate, it was reduced by 2-3% compared to previous years.

(5) Acceptance of Term Bills for Inland Products Merchants who purchase goods from the interior issue term bills that are cashed in major commercial ports and hand them over to the sellers. The sellers discount them at local money houses. In recent years, inland money houses have gradually closed down; even those who are still in business are either weak in capacity or find it difficult to transport cash, and are unwilling to actively accept term bills. Merchants do not dare to carry cash deep into the interior because of the unrest in the interior; therefore, agricultural products are slow to sell, and rural areas are suffering more and more. In view of this, the bank specially ordered its inland branches to do as much discounting and purchasing of term bills as possible. The outstanding balance of discounted and purchased term bills this year increased by more than 2.3 million yuan compared to the previous year; the total number accumulated throughout the year was 43,526,000 yuan, an increase of 10,944,300 yuan compared to the twenty-first year. This is one way to indirectly return capital to the interior. In the past, inland term bills were circulated by money houses; therefore, both the drawer and the seller were accustomed to the money house. The bank purchased the bills discounted by the money house, and the money house was responsible for them, without further research on their origin. Now that the bank directly accepts term bills, it has to deal with both the production and sales sides and be familiar with the actual situation of production and sales.

(6) Assisting in the Completion and Extension of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway was completed at the end of the year to Yushan, with a total length of 355 kilometers. At present, the monthly passenger transport is approximately 100,500 people, and the freight transport is approximately 14,000 tons; compared with the length of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, the passenger transport is slightly more than one-sixth of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, and the freight transport is also slightly more than one-sixth, while the expenditure accounts for slightly less than one-quarter of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. However, due to the economic downturn and the devastation of the communist bandits on the border of Jiangxi, the transportation of goods has not yet been developed. During the Fujian Incident this year, the military transport was fortunately not damaged in the slightest; even the military's travel expenses were issued according to the regulations. Now, the Ministry of Railways and the Jiangxi Provincial Government have decided to extend the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway to carry out the construction of the Yushan-Pingxiang line, and the construction materials will require a total of 16 million yuan. The bank has agreed to undertake the planning in order to complete the starting point of the east-west trunk line south of the Yangtze River, which is necessary to restore the rural economy and improve the knowledge and living standards of farmers. The development of railways is the most urgent task.

The Problem of International Balance of Payments 178

China's annual trade deficits inevitably lead to a point where the shortfall cannot be offset, and the nation's purchasing power and inevitable international income will decline. This has been repeatedly warned to the people in previous reports. This year, the situation has begun to show signs of drying up. The decline in purchasing power can be seen in the significant reduction in this year's trade deficit. The inability to offset the trade deficit is evidenced by the outflow of silver. From the first year of the Republic of China to the twentieth year, except for the period of the European War in the third, fourth, fifth, and sixth years of the Republic of China, when there was a slight surplus, there was almost no year without an import surplus. This was because in previous years, there were intangible import surpluses to compensate. Last year, however, the total of gold and silver showed a greater outflow than inflow. Fortunately, there was a huge export of raw gold, and the import surplus of raw silver was still maintained. However, this year, despite the huge export of raw gold, raw silver actually saw an export surplus of more than 14 million yuan. This is a very rare fact in the history of trade. The export of goods and intangible income are not enough to offset international expenditures, and we are bound to use the savings of currency to offset the deficit. This is an extremely dangerous point in the national economy. Under these circumstances, can our people remain ignorant of the nation's international balance of payments and turn a blind eye to how to balance it?

Estimates of the International Balance of Payments for the Twenty-Second Year

Economists at home and abroad have made various guesses about China's international balance of payments, firstly, because accurate statistics of the figures are not available; secondly, because the balance between income and expenditure cannot be closely approximated. The research office of this bank has recently tried its best to be accurate and approximate within the possible scope from all aspects; however, how can it avoid the aforementioned shortcomings? Now, the estimated figures are described below, as a basis for studying the international balance of payments. This is to draw attention from all parties and provide more accurate data to obtain a complete international balance of payments table, which is also deeply hoped by those who care about the national economy.

1. Value of exported goods: 611,800,000 yuan

2. Underreporting of export values (the declared value of exported goods is generally underreported, conservatively estimated at one-tenth): 61,200,000 yuan

3. Export of raw gold: 189,400,000 yuan

Officially declared exports: 69,400,000 yuan

Smuggled exports (exports from Hong Kong alone have reached 96 million yuan): 120,000,000 yuan

4. Export of raw silver: 14,200,000 yuan

5. Overseas Chinese remittances (reduced by more than one-third this year): 200,000,000 yuan

6. Expenditures of foreigners traveling in China: 10,000,000 yuan

7. Church expenses and charitable donations: 50,000,000 yuan

8. Expenditures of foreign embassies and consulates in China: 30,000,000 yuan

9. Expenditures of foreign troops stationed in China: 100,000,000 yuan

10. Expenditures of foreign ships in China: 25,000,000 yuan

11. Foreign investment and credit expansion in China: 30,000,000 yuan

12. Income from foreign-issued securities owned by Chinese merchants: 5,000,000 yuan

13. Unidentifiable sources: 182,600,000 yuan

Total international income: 1,609,200,000 yuan

1. Value of imported goods: 1,345,600,000 yuan

2. Smuggled imports (smuggling has increased recently due to higher tax rates, conservatively estimated at 10%): 134,600,000 yuan

3. Repayment of foreign debts: 93,000,000 yuan

Customs-guaranteed debt: 75,600,000 yuan

Salt tax-guaranteed debt: 11,400,000 yuan

Railway-guaranteed debt: 6,000,000 yuan

4. Foreign businesses' operating profits (foreign businesses' operations have greatly declined in recent years, and insurance operations are also relatively sluggish, conservatively estimated as follows): 24,000,000 yuan

5. Expenditures of embassies and consulates abroad and study abroad expenses: 6,000,000 yuan

6. Remittances of funds from foreigners in China: 1,000,000 yuan

7. Foreign film rentals: 5,000,000 yuan

Total international expenditures: 1,609,200,000 yuan

According to the above estimated figures, the expenditure is about 160,920,000 yuan, and the income is about 132,660,000 yuan, with a difference of about 28,260,000 yuan. How to compensate for this difference is impossible to prove the source, and we dare not arbitrarily guess. Some say that Chinese people's transactions on the New York Stock Exchange have earned tens of millions, and some say that the deposit of foreign banks in Shanghai has increased by about 90 million yuan, a large part of which is funds that should be remitted but have not been remitted, which also compensates for part of the difference, but we dare not take them as proper data. However, according to the above figures, we can know that the actual income is far less than the actual expenditure, and the large amount of income regarded as a fixed source of overseas Chinese remittances is decreasing day by day. Therefore, the export of raw gold is not enough to make up for the expenditure, and we have to use raw silver to make up for it. This is the most significant phenomenon in the international balance of payments in the 22nd year. Judging from this year to predict next year, the national economy is not far from bankruptcy!

Silver Price Problem

Observing the situation this year, the trend of import surplus is not easy to change, then the increase in the export of silver is inevitable. If the price of silver increases day by day; at the same time, or the price of silver in New York is higher than the exchange value of silver, the rate of increase in exports will be even greater. The rise and fall of silver prices in the past only affected commodity prices; and in the future, the price of silver, due to the relationship of the international balance of payments, will further affect China's silver reserves. The export surplus of raw silver in China seems to have started this year, but in fact, in recent years, there has been no year without an export surplus of raw silver; because Shanghai is almost equal to foreign countries; the difference between the foreign dollars imported into Shanghai and exported abroad is only one step. In the 20th year of the Republic of China, Shanghai's deposit increased by 50 million yuan, in the 21st year, it increased by 126 million yuan, and in the 22nd year, it increased by 109 million yuan; but the import surplus of raw silver was only 45 million yuan in the 20th year, and only 24 million yuan in the 21st year, and the situation in Hong Kong is similar; because the foreign dollars imported into the mainland Shanghai is like preparing to export abroad as the first step. As a result of the concentration of foreign dollars in the mainland commercial ports, currency and credit are shrinking at the same time; resulting in a tragic fall in commodity prices and the decline of the countryside, due to the fall in commodity prices in the mainland. The purchasing power of the people is reduced, and Shanghai's industry and commerce have plummeted; if Shanghai's silver flows out again, then Shanghai's currency and credit will shrink accordingly, and the value of movable and immovable property will fall at the same time; then the silver stored in Shanghai can be changed at any time; that is, the phenomenon that has occurred in the mainland will inevitably reappear in the commercial ports; and the foundation of the national economy is in danger of shaking. If foreign countries take artificial methods again, formulate laws and regulations, and raise the price of silver, it will further promote the export of raw silver. Taking the first half of this year as an example; when preparing for the London Economic Conference, the price of silver rose from 16.5 pence to 20.5 pence, and China purely exported more than 34 million yuan of raw silver; until the price of silver fell back in the second half of the year, there was a slight import, which is one proof. Therefore, for the sake of China, we sincerely hope that all countries will continue the original purpose of stabilizing the price of silver at the London Economic Conference; and we dare not agree with the policy of artificially raising the price excessively. As for saying that raising the price of silver can increase the purchasing power of the Chinese people, I do not know that the purchasing power of the Chinese people has been forced to decline due to the failure to balance the international balance of payments, the contraction of the mainland currency, and the fall in commodity prices. Unless world commodity prices rise and China's exports increase, the purchasing power of the people cannot be restored. The level of the price of silver is already not important. Moreover, all countries have adopted a policy of devaluation and dumping, and if the price of silver is too high, the national goods industry will be greatly affected, which China cannot ignore.

Foreign Credit

The huge difference in the international balance of payments, the remedy is nothing more than increasing production; if you want to increase production, you must have funds for improvement and construction, if you do not import foreign capital and obtain foreign credit, the expenditure to foreign countries will be even greater. Even according to the current trend, without the assistance of foreign credit, it is impossible to maintain the existing purchasing power. However, the acquisition of foreign funds and credit depends on the ability of foreign countries to export capital; and it depends on China's own credit. The thickness of China's own credit depends on the stability of politics and the consolidation of foreign debts. This year, the political situation has become slightly more stable; therefore, the various foreign debts guaranteed by customs duties have all increased, such as the Post-Rehabilitation Bonds, which rose from £73 in January to £90 5 shillings in December; although there is no large-scale plan for railway debts; Fortunately, the old habit of the military requisitioning road funds has been terminated, and various roads can use their remaining strength to consolidate debts, such as the Sino-British company loans of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo and Beijing-Shanghai railways, which stipulate that a certain amount should be repaid monthly, and they have been able to fulfill the plan in the past year; the Fu Company loan of the Daoging Railway has been used to repay the principal and interest monthly; the Beiluo Railway's Big Company loan has paid interest once, the Big Company's part of the continued loan has paid interest once in 28 installments; and the Big Company's part of the original loan has been paid part of the interest in 33 installments; At the same time, the Pinghan British material debt is paid 50,000 yuan per month; the Jinpu British material debt is also paid 50,000 yuan per month; and the Pingui Road's American material debt is paid 5,000 US dollars per month. Although the above are very small amounts; however, it is also the first step to take care of credit. Therefore, this year, the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo bond rose from 84 to more than 90% ; Beijing-Shanghai rose from 41 to 54. If the government can have a comprehensive plan for the consolidation of railway foreign debts; then the credit of railway bonds will not be difficult to increase; China's foreign credit will increase, and the inflow of foreign capital will be easy. This cannot but hope that the government will make further plans. As for the administrative management of state-owned railways in one year this year, there have been improvements, not only are merchants and people benefiting from convenient transportation; it is also of great benefit to the railway's foreign credit!

Rural Relief 179

The Reasons for Rural Decline

In a country where 70-80% of the people are engaged in agriculture, and the rural areas have declined to this extreme, the impact on the national economy is extremely significant; therefore, rural relief is a major problem in the 22nd year, and it has a deep relationship with the financial community. The reasons for the decline of the rural areas are listed in order;

1. The tragic fall in agricultural product prices. The average price of wheat in Jinan, Shandong in the 20th year was 5 yuan 28 cents per dan, and the average price in the 22nd year was 4 yuan 32 cents; the price of rice in Wuhu was 9 yuan 11 cents on average in the 21st year, and 6 yuan 17 cents in the 22nd year; the market price of peanuts in Qingdao fell from the average price of 13 yuan per dan in the 21st year to 9 yuan 50 cents in the 22nd year; the tobacco leaves in Qingzhou, Shandong, were worth 16 yuan 50 cents per dan on average in the 21st year, and only 9 yuan in the 22nd year. According to the wholesale prices in Shanghai investigated by the Tariff Commission, the price of rice in the 22nd year was 55% of that in the 20th year and 81% of that in the 21st year; the price of wheat in the 22nd year was 76% of that in the 20th year and 80% of that in the 21st year; the price of tea in the 22nd year was 43% of that in the 20th year and 59% of that in the 21st year; the price of cocoons in the 22nd year fell 43% compared to the 20th year; the price of peanuts in the 22nd year fell 40% compared to the 20th year and 20% compared to the 21st year; the price of cotton fell the least, and the market price in the 22nd year was 8

Page 18

1% of that in the 20th year and 87% of that in the 21st year. At the same time, the prices of farmers' necessities fell less than the prices of agricultural products. For example, the average price of cotton yarn in the 22nd year fell 24% compared to the 20th year and 9% compared to the 21st year; the price of coarse cloth in the 22nd year fell only 2% compared to the 21st year. According to this calculation, if you exchange a bag of cotton yarn for agricultural products, you only need 19 dan of white rice in the 20th year of the Republic of China; 83 catties of black tea; 142 catties of dried cocoons; 24 dan of peanuts; in the 21st year, you need 23 dan of white rice; 100 catties of black tea; 200 catties of dried cocoons; 27 dan of peanuts; in the 22nd year, you need 26 dan of white rice; 153 catties of black tea; 178 catties of dried cocoons; 31 dan of peanuts. Due to the fall in the price of agricultural products, farmers cannot make ends meet; according to the survey of the Central Agricultural Experimental Institute in Jiangning County; in the 22nd year, the average consumption expenditure of each adult farmer was 52 yuan, and the agricultural income was only 42 yuan, and the amount of income not enough to cover the expenditure was as high as 10 yuan; that is, the amount of income was only 80% of the expenditure.

2. The burden of farmers has increased without decreasing. According to the report of 687 counties of the Central Agricultural Experimental Institute; the tax burden of farmers is still increasing. The total of all provinces; the tax rate of paddy fields was 2.07% of the field price in the 20th year, 2.37% in the 21st year, and 2.68% in the 22nd year, that is, the burden in the 22nd year increased by about 30% compared with the 20th year; the tax rate of dry land was 2.36% of the field price in the 20th year, 2.50% in the 21st year, and 2.80% in the 22nd year, that is, the 22nd year increased by about 20% compared with the 20th year. The landlord's rental income and its burden in Jiangsu Province were examined. In the 20th year, the rental income was 9 yuan, the field tax expenditure was 1 yuan 30 cents, and the remaining amount was 7 yuan 70 cents; in the 21st year, the rental income was 7 yuan 80 cents, the field tax expenditure was 1 yuan 70 cents, and the remaining amount was 6 yuan 10 cents; in the 22nd year, the rental income was 7 yuan 40 cents, the field tax expenditure was 2 yuan 70 cents, and the remaining amount was 4 yuan 70 cents; therefore, landlords invested in buying fields, and in the 20th year, they got a weekly interest of 7.7%; in the 21st year, they got 6.1%; and in the 22nd year, they only got 4.7%.

3. The repercussions of the fall in the price of foreign agricultural products. Although the import quantity of foreign agricultural products in the 22nd year was slightly less than that in the 21st year; however, its low price not only threatened the price of Chinese agricultural products at all times, making it impossible to rise; the quantity imported into China has indirectly overwhelmed Chinese agricultural products. The US cotton and wheat loans also have a great impact on the price of cotton and wheat in China.

4. The lack of abundant agricultural harvests. China's agricultural harvests are not abundant, firstly because the area of arable land is not large; secondly because of the degradation of production methods. The total arable land in the country is 1,462,682 square li; but the arable land is only 322,443 square li, accounting for 22%. The harvest of foreign wheat is abundant, with each hectare counting as 100 kilos, Canada is 10.9; the United States is 9.9; Australia is 7.4; China is 7.3. The harvest of rice is 34.2 in Japan; 46.4 in Italy; 22.9 in Taiwan; and 18.9 in China (the above are the averages from 1928 to 1931). In the 20th year of the Republic of China, the harvest of grain was 1,558,000,000 dan, in the 21st year it was 1,698,000,000 dan, and in the 22nd year it was 1,586,000,000 dan; that is, it only increased by 2% compared to the previous year, and it was 6% less than last year; the cotton output in the 22nd year was 20% more than in the 20th year and 35% more than in the 21st year; but the reason for the increase in output was due to the increase in the planting area. Not an increase in production.

Due to the decline of the rural areas, the value of agricultural land is declining day by day. In total, the price of paddy fields fell by 6% last year compared to the previous year, and this year it fell by 12% compared to the previous year; the price of dry land fell by 7% last year and 11% this year. Therefore, the land in the north that used to be worth 150 yuan per mu is now depreciated to 30 or 40 yuan, and no one cares about it; the south has also fallen by almost half the price, and there is still no owner; causing it extremely difficult for farmers to mortgage their land for cash. In the past, the heavy interest burden of farmers' loans was criticized by the world, but today, even with heavy interest, it is difficult to borrow cash.

Relief Measures

Knowing the reasons for the decline of the rural areas, it is nothing more than that the operating costs of farmers are high and the value obtained is low; that is, knowing that to relieve the rural areas, on the one hand, we must reduce agricultural costs; on the other hand, we must increase the prices of agricultural products.

This year, the government and society have taken measures to reduce agricultural costs and increase agricultural product prices;

1. The government issued a general order to abolish excessive taxes and miscellaneous taxes; but various provinces have not yet taken concrete actions to reduce or abolish them.

2. Financial institutions advocated loans to farmers; various banks either set up agricultural warehouses to try out small loans; or advocated indirect loans from cooperatives; but the total amount was less than six or seven million yuan. The interest rate was reduced to between 1% and 8%.

3. The government levied import taxes on foreign rice at one gold unit per dan, which is equivalent to 1 yuan 95 cents in foreign currency; the import tax on foreign wheat is 0.30 gold units per dan, which is equivalent to 59 cents in foreign currency; the import tax on foreign flour is 0.75 gold units per dan, which is equivalent to 1 yuan 47 cents in foreign currency; however, Guangdong, Guangxi and Fujian, where foreign rice is imported the most, have not yet implemented the levy. 4. Financial institutions added warehouses to increase agricultural product pledges.

As for the central and provincial agencies that handle agricultural improvement, the number is as follows;

Administration and Design 46

Experimentation and Research 161

Promotion 307

Agricultural Finance 58

However, the various agencies run are all limited by limited funds, narrow scale, limited strength, and slow progress. In addition, the increase in the number of cooperatives is worth mentioning. The types are listed in the table as follows;

The governments of all countries are using all their national strength to relieve agriculture by various methods; and the decline of China's rural areas has reached this extreme, and the relief measures are only as described above. For the future of the national economy, we cannot but be deeply worried; that is, like a weak body, we must apply heavy tonics, and empty talk about hygiene and minor medicines cannot bring the dead back to life. If the central and local governments can jointly raise tens of millions of huge funds, and have a cooperative organization; at the same time, consolidating the field tax and surtax, and moderately reducing it, may be able to gradually save it. Our sad and painful Manchuria, the so-called central bank, is still using 12 million yuan to provide low-interest loans to support spring plowing, one yuan per mu. How can China's size be saved by hundreds of millions of yuan? As for commercial financial institutions, although it is not impossible to slightly fulfill the responsibility of promoting; however, after all, it cannot be completely guaranteed by land and credit to save the most urgent and poorest farmers; therefore, thorough relief will not be successful without the government's actual subsidy. On the social side, we can only urgently cultivate personnel who serve rural work and encourage young people who have already received considerable education to engage in rural work. We in the financial community hope that the banks will continue their existing work, promote the popularization of cooperatives, and assist in improving transportation and sales, which is also fulfilling their share of responsibility!

The Agricultural Production and Import of Agricultural Products in the 22nd Year 180

According to various statistics on the grain harvest of the 22nd year of the Republic, the national average total was 6% less than in the 21st year, but 2% more than in the 20th year. Specifically: In the Northwest region, namely the five provinces of Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Gansu, and Shaanxi, the wheat harvest was 25% less than in the 20th year and 9% less than in the 21st year; the coarse grains harvest was 10% more than in the 20th year and 8% more than in the 21st year. Combined, the total was 5% less than in the 20th year. In the Northern region, namely the four provinces of Shanxi, Hebei, Shandong, and Henan, the wheat harvest was 11% more than in the 20th year and 10% more than in the 21st year; the coarse grains harvest was 3% less than in the 20th year and 8% less than in the 21st year; the sweet potato harvest was 36% more than in the 20th year and 20% more than in the 21st year. Combined, the total was 3% more than in the 20th year and 1% less than in the 21st year. In the Central region, namely the three provinces of Hubei, Hunan, and Jiangxi, the wheat harvest was 4% less than in the 20th year and 10% less than in the 21st year; the rice harvest was 4% more than in the 20th year and 11% less than in the 21st year; the coarse grains and sweet potato harvest was 40% more than during the floods of the 20th year and 6% less than in the 21st year. Combined, the total grain harvest was 4% more than the flood year and 13% less than last year. In the Eastern region, namely the three provinces of Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, the wheat harvest was 11% less than the year before; the rice harvest was 26% more than in the 20th year and 3% more than in the 21st year; the sweet potato harvest also increased. Combined, the total was 30% more than in the 20th year and 1% more than in the 21st year. In the Southwest region, namely the three provinces of Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou, the wheat harvest was 4% less than in the 20th year and 11% less than in the 21st year; the rice harvest was 10% less than in the 20th year and 10% less than in the 21st year; the coarse grains and sweet potato harvest was 9% less than in the 20th year and 13% more than in the 21st year. Combined, the total was 9% less than in the 20th year and 17% less than in the 21st year. In the Southeast region, namely the two provinces of Fujian and Guangdong, the rice harvest was 5% less than in the 20th year and 6% less than in the 21st year; the sweet potatoes and wheat harvest was similar to the previous two years. Combined, the total was 3% less than in the 20th year and 5% less than in the 21st year.

Cotton: In the 22nd year, the national cotton crop benefited from favorable rainfall during planting and suitable weather during germination, resulting in vigorous growth. Furthermore, stability gradually returned to the northern provinces, leading to increased cotton acreage and production, particularly in Shanxi and Hubei. Minor damage was limited to small areas along the Yellow River in Shandong and the Yangtze River in Hubei, as well as the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, which experienced some wind and rain damage. According to a survey by the China Cotton Association, the national cotton acreage totaled 40,453,953 mu, an increase of 8,816,174 mu compared to the 20th year and 3,354,153 mu compared to the 21st year, representing increases of 28% and 9%, respectively. The national cotton production amounted to 9,621,240 dan, an increase of 3,221,460 dan compared to the 20th year and 1,515,603 dan compared to the 21st year, representing increases of 50% and 19%, respectively. The significant increase in production was the largest since the 8th year of the Republic.

Tea: The most prominent tea-producing regions include the provinces of Jiangxi, Anhui, Fujian, Hunan, Hubei, and Zhejiang. In recent years, due to factors such as decreased sales and frequent banditry, tea production has significantly declined. Accurate statistics on China's tea planting area and tea production are unavailable. However, according to a rough estimate by the Ministry of Industry, the tea planting area is around 3 million mu, and the tea production is between 4 million and 5 million dan. It can be confidently stated that both the tea planting area and production are declining year by year. According to customs reports, the export value was over 51.8 million yuan in the 20th year, over 38.5 million yuan in the 21st year, and only over 34.2 million yuan in the 22nd year.

Tobacco: According to surveys, this year's tobacco production increased by 25% compared to the 21st year, amounting to approximately 1.04 million dan. Shandong had the highest production, reaching 470,000 dan, an increase of 40,000 dan compared to last year. The tobacco-producing areas of the province experienced favorable rainfall, resulting in plump and large tobacco leaves, with a yield of 250 jin per mu. The planted acreage in Henan and Anhui also increased, and the tobacco varieties were also good. However, the price dropped sharply, causing hardship for the villagers. Silkworm Cocoons: In the 22nd year, the spring silkworm cocoon production was approximately 110,000 dan, the summer cocoon production was approximately 30,000 dan, and the autumn cocoon production was approximately 40,000 dan, totaling 180,000 dan, which was an increase compared to the 21st year.

Peanuts: According to estimates by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station of the Ministry of Industry, this year's peanut production was 170,000 dan in Shanxi, 6,350,000 dan in Hebei, 13,760,000 dan in Shandong, and 4,820,000 dan in Henan, totaling 25,100,000 dan.

Vegetable Oil: This year's soybean oil exports were nearly zero (because the customs of the three northeastern provinces are not counted). The export value in the 21st year had already decreased by two-thirds compared to the 20th year, but there were still more than 460,000 dan, worth more than 7.48 million yuan. In the 22nd year, the export amount was only one dan, worth 23 yuan. However, the export volume of tung oil slightly increased compared to the 21st year, amounting to 1,246,847 dan, totaling 30,261,269 yuan. The export volume in the previous year was 802,769 dan, worth 23,316,233 yuan.

Import of Agricultural Products: Despite the abundant agricultural harvest in the 22nd year, the import of agricultural products still reached a substantial 400 million yuan. The largest category was rice, amounting to 150 million yuan, only a decrease of 35 million yuan compared to the 21st year. Cotton amounted to 98 million yuan, a decrease of 87 million yuan compared to the 21st year. Wheat amounted to 87 million yuan, a decrease of 3 million yuan compared to the 21st year. Flour amounted to 27 million yuan, a decrease of half compared to the 21st year. Tobacco amounted to 26 million yuan, a decrease of 10 million yuan compared to the 21st year. Sugar amounted to 42 million yuan, a decrease of 30 million yuan compared to the 21st year. However, due to the increase in import tariffs last year, the amount of smuggled imports was also not small. The comparison of the import value of agricultural products and the total import value in the past three years is as follows:

Year Import Export Total Trade Deficit

The only countries with increased imports were Australia and the Soviet Union. The Soviet Union was the largest dumper of tobacco and oil, while Australia was the major importer of wheat and flour. With regard to exports, the future of trade with the United States is promising. Steel, machinery, vehicles, timber, etc., will inevitably increase year by year due to China's construction needs and the low exchange rate of the US dollar. Before China increases the production of improved cotton varieties, the raw materials for fine cotton yarn will still have to rely on the United States. Therefore, the situation of trade deficit will inevitably continue. The only way to make up for this trade deficit is to increase the export of tung oil, raw silk, and fur, and to find ways to promote the export of other agricultural products.

Whether China's agricultural products are sufficient for self-sufficiency cannot be determined with accurate statistics. However, considering the situation of rice reserves in the mainland, it cannot be said that it is not self-sufficient. Only by ensuring average distribution and improving marketing can the supply of rice in various regions be increased. Moreover, the provinces that import large quantities of foreign rice are only Fujian and Guangdong. If the rice-producing provinces along the Yangtze River can establish an improved

marketing system with Fujian and Guangdong, reducing transportation costs, and with the support of the government's strength, it will not be difficult to achieve results. Currently, cotton production is indeed insufficient to meet the needs of various yarn factories, especially the insufficient production of fine cotton yarn, requiring the import of about 300,000 bales of foreign cotton each year. However, fine American cotton can be produced in western Henan, eastern Qi, and central Shaanxi. If the government fully encourages this, production can be increased year by year, and the import of foreign cotton will naturally decrease. As for wheat and flour, China's production can still be self-sufficient, and only by improving marketing can factories avoid purchasing foreign wheat. The most difficult thing is sugar, because the import of foreign sugar has resulted in a daily decrease in the planting of sugar raw materials such as sugarcane and beets. Now, promoting sugar production must start with promoting the planting of raw materials. One thing must be said: if China wants to curb the increase in imports of agricultural products, it must seek fundamental improvements in agriculture. However, superficial solutions should not be abandoned. I believe that increasing import tariffs is an effective way to promote agricultural self-sufficiency at present. For example, after Jiangsu and Zhejiang increased the import tax on foreign rice in the 22nd year, the import of foreign rice greatly decreased. If the import tariff rate can be improved simultaneously with the improvement of production and marketing, gradually increasing it, then domestic production can be self-sufficient. The import tariff rate for wheat and flour is only 0.30 gold units per dan, equivalent to 0.586 yuan, which is far from the 2.25 yuan per dan of wheat levied by Japan. If the import tax on wheat is increased to one gold unit and flour is increased to 1.50 gold units, it will not be far from the Japanese tax rate. Because China can produce enough wheat and flour, a slight increase in tax rate will not greatly affect the people's food. Although cotton cannot be self-sufficient, if a considerable import tax can be levied, the price of Chinese cotton will increase, and farmers will naturally increase planting cotton. Even if the price of fine yarn is worried about being raised due to taxation, reducing the consumption of fine yarn may also be a way to encourage thrift. Therefore, in order to save the rural decline and promote agricultural self-sufficiency, it is hoped that the government will give careful consideration to the import tariff on agricultural products. Even for friendly countries that have trade relations with China, only by China's early recovery of agriculture can the purchasing power of the Chinese people be improved, which they should also sympathize with.

International Trade in the 22nd Year 181

In the 22nd year, the import trade volume was over 134.5 million yuan, and the export trade volume was over 61.1 million yuan, totaling over 195.7 million yuan. The trade deficit was over 73.3 million yuan. Compared with the 21st year, imports decreased by 18%, exports decreased by 20%, and the trade deficit also decreased by 15%. Taking the 18th year as the standard, the annual decline index is as follows: (taking the 18th year as 100)

The increase was in the United States, Hong Kong, and Annam. The increase in the United States was due to the strong sales of tung oil and wool; the increase in Hong Kong was due to the increased transshipment of mineral sand and raw silk; the increase in Annam was only several tens of thousands of yuan. The index compared with the 21st year is as follows: (taking the 21st year as 100)

In the 22nd year, the countries that had the main trade relations with China were the United States, the United Kingdom, and Japan, which are described below:

United States: In recent years, due to good international relations and convenient transportation, the United States has been able to maintain its superior position in trade with China. In the 22nd year, the import volume decreased significantly, from 41,937,500 yuan to 29,746,800 yuan, accounting for 21.86% of China's total import value, a decrease of 3.57% compared to the 21st year. What China relies on the United States for are cotton, flour, tobacco, kerosene, gasoline, and timber, most of which are raw materials. Although Soviet Russian oil competes with kerosene and gasoline, it has not decreased and still ranks first in imports, amounting to over 75.9 million yuan. Due to China's abundant cotton production and decreased sales of cotton yarn, cotton decreased from over 15.6 million yuan last year to over 6.65 million yuan. Due to China's abundant tobacco harvest and increased unified tax on cigarettes, cigarette factories tend to use low-priced Chinese raw materials, which decreased from over 36 million yuan last year to over 26 million yuan. The price of American flour cannot compete with Australia, so the import of American wheat is almost extinct. Flour decreased from over 34 million yuan last year to over 11 million yuan. Timber slightly increased. In addition, airplanes and vehicles increased significantly. The main goods that China imports from the United States are tung oil, and exports increased from over 14 million yuan last year to over 21 million yuan. Hide and skin increased from over 14 million yuan last year to over 20 million yuan. Wool increased the most significantly, from over 1.7 million yuan last year to over 11 million yuan this year. China's trade with the United States: imports were 29,746,800 yuan; exports were 11,314,600 yuan, a difference of 18,432,200 yuan. Observation in China

United Kingdom: As a result of excluding Japanese goods, British import trade jumped from third to second place. This year's imports decreased from 18,570,000 yuan to 15,400,000 yuan, a decrease of 17% compared to last year, accounting for 11.33% of China's total import value, with little difference from last year. The main imports are hardware, cotton cloth, machinery, wool fabric, yarn, and ammonium sulfate. Due to the competition of Japanese goods, the progress of China's domestic industry, and the increase of Chinese tax rates, the import of cotton cloth decreased from more than 36 million yuan last year to more than 19 million yuan. Hardware increased from more than 22 million yuan to more than 29 million yuan due to the increase of railway construction and the need for materials for domestic industry. Machinery and tools decreased by more than 3 million yuan due to the decline of the market and the lack of expansion of various industries. Wool fabrics and yarn slightly decreased, with little change. Ammonium sulfate also decreased. The main goods that China exports to the United Kingdom are eggs, tea, bristles, alpaca wool, straw hats, tung oil, and wool carpets. Eggs decreased from more than 24.5 million yuan last year to more than 21.9 million yuan, a decrease of 11%. Tea decreased from 4.57 million yuan to 3.84 million yuan. Pig bristles decreased from 2.96 million yuan to 2.51 million yuan. Straw hats and wool carpets slightly increased. From the above, we can know that China's exports to the United Kingdom are very small. The export value decreased from 58.5 million yuan last year to 48.76 million yuan, with a trade deficit of more than 10.527 million yuan. With the progress of China's construction and the increase in railway construction, the reliance on the United Kingdom for hardware, machinery, and railway materials will inevitably increase day by day, while there are few goods that China can supply to the United Kingdom. This is a problem that Chinese and British people should study.

Japan: Japan's trade with China has greatly decreased due to the impact of excluding Japanese goods and the exclusion of trade volume in the Northeast. Imports were 13.2 million yuan, accounting for 9.71% of the total import value, a decrease of more than 98.8 million yuan compared to the 21st year, a decrease of 42.8%. The main imports were cotton textiles, sugar, various machines, chemical products, seafood, metal products, paper, coal, and rubber products. Exports decreased from 16,746,000 yuan last year to 9,580,000 yuan. The share of China's total exports decreased from 21.80% to 15.65%. The main exports were cotton, followed by cotton yarn, mostly exported by Japanese factories in China, accounting for more than 13 million yuan; bran accounted for more than 5.9 million yuan; kernels accounted for more than 8.16 million yuan; seed cake and miscellaneous grain products accounted for more than 4.79 million yuan; accounted for more than 4.12 million yuan; the rest were metal ore, pig bristles, frozen meat, hides, etc., which were very small. However, if Japan's trade with China includes the Northeast, it will increase greatly. What Japan has lost in China has been recovered in the Northeast, and what China has lost can no longer be recovered! Japan's import trade deficit is more than 36 million yuan. Although the current trade deficit does not seem to be large, Japanese goods are being dumped at low prices this year, which has gradually taken effect. It is feared that the trade deficit next year will be greater than this year's.

In addition, other places that are more related are Hong Kong, Australia, Germany, India, etc. In addition to its own trade, Hong Kong is also a place for China to transfer trade with other countries. The value of goods imported from Hong Kong to China was 48.28 million yuan; the value of goods imported from China to Hong Kong was 120.95 million yuan. Therefore, the value of goods imported from China to Hong Kong ranks first in China's exports, accounting for 19.75% of the total export value. The main commodities were mineral sand, tin ingots, etc., worth more than 20 million yuan, silk fabrics and cloth worth more than 12 million yuan, which is the result of the progress of domestic industry; poultry and livestock worth more than 7.9 million yuan; medicinal materials and fragrant villages worth 7 million yuan; cotton yarn worth 4.7 million yuan; embroidered goods worth 4.3 million yuan; fruits worth 1.6 million yuan; peanut oil worth 2.7 million yuan; tung oil worth 2.6 million yuan; In addition, peanuts, seafood, fresh eggs, tea, paper, etc., totaled more than 59 million yuan. The main commodities imported from Hong Kong were sugar worth more than 9.3 million yuan; fish and seafood worth 6.8 million yuan; medicinal materials and fragrant materials worth 4.3 million yuan; others were sandalwood, rice, pigments, books, wool fabrics, etc., more than 100 kinds, worth 72 million yuan in total. Therefore, Hong Kong trade has a value of attention in China's trade, and it is necessary to maintain good relations. Australian wheat accounts for 80% of imported foreign wheat. Its import value increased from 63.5 million yuan last year to 85.7 million yuan. The value of German imports has been increasing year by year. On the Indian side, exports slightly increased.

In summary, 80 to 90 percent of China's exports are agricultural products. To reduce the trade deficit, it is necessary to reduce the export of agricultural products and increase the export of agricultural products. The export volume of agricultural products in the past three years and their value are as follows:

Year Total Value of Main Agricultural Exports

Republic of China 20th Year 421,000,000 yuan

Republic of China 21st Year X 253,000,000 yuan

Republic of China 22nd Year X 241,000,000 yuan

X The 21st year of the Republic of China only includes the figures from January to June in the Northeast ports, and the figures in the 22nd year of the Republic of China do not include the figures in the Northeast ports at all.

The total value of main agricultural exports has been decreasing year by year in the past three years. One is the elimination of bulk agricultural products in the Northeast; the second is the global recession, and countries have increased taxes to restrict imports; and the third is the low market price, and the sales and sales value of China's agricultural products are decreasing day by day. Under this situation, to increase the export of agricultural products, in terms of fundamental solutions, it is necessary to improve quality, unify types, and reduce costs. In terms of superficial solutions, the main exported agricultural products should be exempt from export taxes. It is true that this kind of export tax is unique in the world. The government should pay attention to the national economy and should not care about these tens of millions of yuan of income.

The State of Industry in the Twenty-Second Year 182

Among China's industries that developed relatively early and on a broader scale, the most prominent were cotton mills, flour mills, and silk factories. Next were the cigarette and match industries. The emerging industries with a smaller scope were daily necessities. The progress of flour mills has reached a considerable limit, while cotton mills have expanded annually. However, due to the weak purchasing power of the people and narrow sales channels, cotton and flour mills that are not managed effectively are facing losses. The silk industry is struggling to survive due to falling silk prices. The cigarette and match industries face fierce competition and high consolidated taxes. Except for a few firmly established businesses, most find it difficult to profit. As for the emerging daily necessities industry, which was in the autumn of development and growth, it showed signs of difficulty and decline last year. This was due to the impact of the January 28th Incident and the decline of rural areas. Therefore, from the perspective of the entire industry, the twenty-second year can be considered the beginning of a difficult period for the industrial sector. Regionally, factories in the interior, close to raw material production areas and consumer markets, have lower costs than those in treaty ports. Thus, the cotton and flour mills in the interior performed better than those in Shanghai, Tianjin, and Hankou this year. However, Chinese industries in both the interior and concession areas are constantly threatened by the competition from foreign factories established in China and the dumping of similar imported foreign goods. This is a persistent concern for those engaged in industrial management.

Textile Industry

The sharp decline in cotton yarn prices in the twenty-second year was unprecedented in the last decade. In the twenty-first year, the lowest price of standard yarn was 193 yuan, while in the current year, it was 166 yuan. This year, the sales volume of Shanghai merchant guilds was only 70% of the twenty-first year and less than half of the twentieth year. Compared with the nineteenth year before the disasters, sales in the South and the Yangtze River region decreased by half, while in the North, they decreased by only one-fiftieth. According to the statistics in March of the twenty-second year, the total number of yarn spindles in the country was 5,019,917, an increase of 322,637 compared to last year and 575,617 compared to the year before. Under these circumstances, each had to seek survival. Consequently, foreign cotton mills competed with Chinese cotton mills, interior cotton mills competed with treaty port cotton mills, and northern cotton mills competed with southern cotton mills. The more intense the competition, the more difficult the survival. Generally speaking, most cotton mills across the country suffered losses, with even those making a slight profit faring much worse than last year. Comparing Japanese cotton mills with Chinese cotton mills, the cost of Japanese yarn decreased more and more, and the quality of products improved daily. Furthermore, they had outlets in Southeast Asia and India, which Chinese cotton mills could not hope to match. Comparing interior cotton mills with those in treaty ports, interior cotton mills found workers easier to train and manage, resulting in higher work efficiency. Additionally, they were either close to consumer markets or raw material production areas, giving them a considerable advantage over treaty port factories. Northern cotton mills had always relied on the Northeast as a major outlet, but recently, this route has been cut off, making business even more difficult than for southern cotton mills. However, according to the principle of survival of the fittest, the more intense the competition, the faster the improvement. Those lacking knowledge and with corrupt management will naturally be eliminated, while those with excellent technology and rational management will survive. Analyzing Chinese cotton mills in the current year reveals significant differences. Given China's large population, these five million spindles account for approximately one per hundred people. Japan, with a population of sixty million, still has eight million spindles. Therefore, the future of China's cotton industry should not be considered as having reached its peak. At the same time, domestic cotton cloth is easier to compete with foreign goods due to the gradual increase in import tariffs, providing protection. Therefore, for Chinese cotton mills, it is advisable to strive to reduce costs and improve production to strengthen their competitiveness. On the one hand, they should choose inland areas with higher yarn sales or more convenient raw material supply to establish factories and avoid pressure from foreign factories. Now, the Cotton Industry Control Association is actively working on cotton planting improvement, ensuring a more sufficient supply of raw materials in the interior. This should not be ignored by those engaged in the cotton yarn business. The comparison between Chinese and Japanese cotton mills is as follows:

Factory Number Chinese Japanese

Flour Milling Industry

Flour mills are concentrated in the South, with the Northeast being the largest destination, followed by the North. Domestic flour sales to the Northeast were approximately four million bags, but recently, they have been no more than tens of thousands of bags. The North has seen the dumping of cheap Japanese and Russian flour, impacting local flour mills in Tianjin. The destination routes for southern flour mills are even narrower due to unrest in the Guangdong area, weak purchasing power among the people, and merchants' reluctance to stockpile goods. Especially this year, with abundant wheat harvests in various regions, rural farmers are consuming flour ground locally, further hindering flour sales. At the same time, the establishment of American flour and wheat loans coincided with the new wheat harvest season, leading to a sharp drop in flour prices to a decades-low, from 2.67 yuan to around 2 yuan. Factories' inventories piled up, with Shanghai's highest inventory reaching over 3 million bags. Tianjin and Hankou also had over 2 million bags. As a last resort, factories announced shutdowns after the Mid-Autumn Festival. Later, to provide for workers' livelihoods, they operated in shifts. Among those that closed were Minfeng in Tianjin and Lifeng in Ningbo. Generally speaking, for the flour industry this year, raw material and flour prices fell simultaneously. Those who produced and sold immediately could mostly profit. Unlike the yarn industry, which faces foreign competition, as long as one acts cautiously, there should be no major losses. Recently, the imposition of import tariffs on foreign flour provides manufacturers with some breathing room.

Silk Reeling Industry

Silk reelers in the twenty-second year acted cautiously due to the majority of losses in the previous year. Even farmers raising silkworms dared not expand. Fortunately, the weather was favorable, resulting in a larger cocoon yield and relatively stable cocoon prices. After manufacturers purchased spring cocoons, silk prices suddenly rose, allowing for some profit. However, with the second harvest in summer and autumn, cocoon prices increased while foreign silk markets steadily declined, causing manufacturers to turn profits into losses. Although exports this year increased by 18% compared to last year, the drop in silk prices was more severe than last year. In the American market, silk prices reached a high of 895 yuan and a low of 640 yuan last year. This year, the high was 990 yuan, but the low was only around 500 yuan. Moreover, the highest price was merely a flash in the pan. According to this year's figures, Japanese silk production increased by 9.2%, equivalent to 50,000 piculs, while American consumption decreased by 84,000 piculs. At the same time, the production of rayon is increasing daily. Given the small quantity, high cost, poor quality, and unsound marketing system of Chinese raw silk, its inability to stand its ground under the pressure of these global trends is self-evident. This year, the average cost of spring and autumn cocoons was 700 yuan. Adding reeling wages and other expenses of about 150 yuan, the cost per picul reached over 800 yuan. However, silk prices fell to over 500 yuan, resulting in losses for most silk reelers. Among the silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, totaling over 110, only 5 or 6 factories in Shanghai, a dozen in Wuxi, and 6 or 7 in Zhejiang continued operating by the end of the year, less than one-fifth. Therefore, the decline of the silk industry has reached a critical stage. In the future, it will be impossible to save it without improving raw materials, advancing technology, and fundamentally reforming. The path to improving raw materials and advancing technology can only succeed through modern scientific methods, not through the old-fashioned, piecemeal remedies. Now, there is a Silk Industry Improvement Committee dedicated to fundamental improvement. There is no shortage of people in the silk industry with new knowledge who are using modern methods for management and working hard. It cannot be said that there is no hope of revival.

Cigarette Industry

In recent years, the sales of domestic cigarettes have gradually increased, and the establishment of Chinese cigarette factories has surged, reaching as many as 156. However, only a few have a larger scale and complete equipment. This year, due to the increase in consolidated taxes, the prevalence of locally produced cigarettes in various regions, and the weak purchasing power of the people, business in various factories has been far worse than before. Small factories have closed down one after another, and now only about 50 or 60 remain. In the twentieth year, the consolidated taxes paid by Chinese factories were higher than those paid by British-American Tobacco companies. In the twenty-first year, they were roughly equal. This year, they were lower than those paid by British-American Tobacco. In the future, the inability of small factories to survive and the need for large factories to improve are clear trends. What is worth studying is that the confrontation between Chinese cigarette factories and British-American Tobacco companies is similar to the relationship between Chinese cotton mills and Japanese cotton mills. However, the Shanxi Provincial Government has self-managed cigarette factories and promotes its products with the power of the government. Currently, the monthly sales of British-American Tobacco in Shanxi cannot exceed one-third of the sales of the Shanxi self-managed cigarette factories. The Shandong Provincial Government has also recently introduced measures to encourage the products of Chinese self-managed cigarette factories. This is one aspect of a new trend in the cigarette industry.

Match Industry

The Chinese match industry has gradually declined since the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. By the eighteenth and nineteenth years, it was in a precarious state. However, after the implementation of increased tariffs in January of the twentieth year, the import of foreign matches decreased, and Chinese manufacturers gradually saw a turnaround. This year was the most stable year for business. Starting from the twenty-first year, the industry re-entered a bleak period, and various factories lowered prices one after another. This year, larger factories can still survive, while smaller factories are in extreme distress. The main reason is the unlimited production volume of each factory. For example, in the eighteenth year, the output was only 600,000 boxes. It increased to 700,000 boxes in the nineteenth year and returned to 600,000 boxes in the twentieth year. However, it suddenly increased to 730,000 boxes in the twenty-first year. However, the imported foreign matches that decreased due to the increased tariffs were only over 50,000 boxes. Ignoring sales, each factory arbitrarily increased production, leading to price competition. The selling price of 53 or 4 yuan per box in the past is now only 40 yuan. The selling price of 20 yuan in the past is now only about 12 yuan. The selling price only covers the cost or even falls below the cost. Therefore, if the match industry itself does not quickly unite and limit production, it is feared that all will be unable to sustain themselves. There are over 50 match factories nationwide. Foreign merchants have established seven factories, but their output accounts for about a quarter of that of Chinese factories, indicating that strong competitors to Chinese match factories still exist.

Daily Necessities Industry

Rubber Industry:

Due to the increase in new factories, overproduction, and accumulated inventory, the value of goods has fallen. Top-quality overshoes, which used to sell for 11 or 12 yuan per dozen, have now dropped to 8 or 9 yuan. Inferior goods from small factories sell for just over 5 yuan. It is rumored that there are over 4 million pairs in stock. Among the 50 or so rubber factories in Shanghai, large and small, more than one-fifth have suspended or ceased operations this year. Among the remaining two-thirds, only 6 or 7 are doing relatively well.

Cosmetics Industry:

There are 40 or 50 factories. The total business volume this year should be around 7 million yuan. Six or seven larger factories are still making profits, while smaller ones are just breaking even.

Soap Industry:

It has also developed significantly in recent years, with 50 or so factories, large and small. However, only a dozen or so have a larger scale. Their products are not only sold domestically but also exported to Southeast Asia.

Enamelware Industry:

There are a dozen or so factories in Shanghai. Business this year has been average, with a total volume of approximately 4 million yuan.

Acid Production:

It is one of the emerging industries in recent years. There are currently two acid production plants.

Electric Battery Industry:

There are a dozen or so establishments. Larger ones can produce 15,000 batteries per day, while smaller ones produce between 2,000 and 7,000. Approximately 1.3 million batteries can be produced each month, with an annual output of 12 to 13 million batteries. Annual imports of Japanese goods are about 6 to 7 million batteries. Foreign factories in China also produce 6 to 7 million batteries. However, China's total annual demand is only 16 to 17 million batteries, leading to oversupply. Coupled with the dumping of cheap foreign goods, it is difficult for various factories to profit.

Knitting Industry:

There are over 200 factories, large and small, in Shanghai. Business this year has decreased by approximately 38%.

Food Seasoning Industry:

There are too many factories, leading to fierce price competition. Several have been unable to sustain themselves and have closed down. The total business volume for the year is only 3 to 4 million yuan.

Woolen Fabric Industry:

It has recently shown slight signs of growth. The business of the Tianjin Dongya Factory is still good.

In addition, the business volume of industries such as alkali production, mechanized stone powder, and mercerized cotton weaving is not significant and does not vary greatly.

China's industry has shown some glimmer of hope in recent years. However, due to the decline of rural areas, the impact of the global recession, the pressure from foreign merchants establishing factories in China, and the reckless competition among businesses, this budding industry is facing the risk of setbacks and stagnation. It is hoped that the industrial sector will thoroughly realize this, jointly work to improve technology, eliminate reckless competition, and that the government will supervise technological improvement and restrict reckless competition. This will demonstrate the effectiveness of unified national implementation of controls. The future of industry will be promising.

Industrial Control and Inflation 183

Economic control and inflation have become major tools for various countries to protect property and relieve people's livelihoods. The officials and people of our country, alarmed by the decline of industry and the pressure of foreign goods, are vigorously advocating for imitation. Initially, the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, together with the silk industry and financial sector, established the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silkworm Silk Control Committee. Next, the Economic Commission established the Cotton Industry Control Committee. In addition, the Shanxi Provincial Government established an economic control research institution to prepare various control plans. Given the shallow knowledge of the Chinese people and the weak foundation of emerging industries, it would be as difficult as waiting for the Yellow River to clear to expect the nation to awaken and act on its own to revive the economy. If we take the established rules of control in various countries as the only shortcut to saving China's industry, we fear that it will not only fail to be effective but may also hinder the progress of industrial development. The industrial controls of various countries are mostly due to overproduction after industrial development, while China's problem lies in the degradation and inadequacy of production. Therefore, various countries are focusing on the control of prices, sales, production volume, and demand. What China should pay attention to is the control of variety and grade. Improving variety and grade depends on the production education of farmers and the technical education of workers. These are the common basic conditions for the development of industries in various countries, and no country can skip steps. Industrial control is not impossible, but the stages of implementation must be distinguished. It is appropriate to start with the control of product varieties and, on the other hand, to promote the universalization of production education and vocational education. The scope of control should be limited to what can be managed with political power. The implementation of control should be shifted according to the preparation of statistics and talents. Some also advocate trade control. The so-called trade control intends to increase exports and reduce imports. However, the preconditions are whether there are exports with excellent quality and uniform grades, and whether there is a sufficient supply. Otherwise, even if there is demand but no supply, control is impossible. Those who advocate for inflation believe that low agricultural product prices and a lack of production funds can be addressed by increasing the amount of funds and raising agricultural product prices through the mechanism of inflation. Some also advocate reducing the fineness of currency to achieve the goal of inflation and to resist the excessive increase in the price of silver in the United States. Those with some economic knowledge can explain the role of inflation. However, there is a premise: does China already have a sound currency system? It is like having perfect machinery to fully utilize its effectiveness. Today, the non-uniform fineness and prices of China's subsidiary currencies and the lack of a system for bank-issued paper money mean that the credibility of silver dollars after the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan is still in the testing phase. Therefore, what the people trust is the substance of the currency, not the currency that represents the substance. The credit of currency has not been established. How can we fully utilize its elastic function? Therefore, the theory of inflation is not impossible, but establishing a sound currency system is a prerequisite. The Chinese people regard discussions about currency system reform as stale rhetoric. If this basic work is not carried out, even if various countries have good methods and intentions, they cannot be transferred to China. Presenting theories is no different from drooling over the butcher's shop without buying meat. It is hoped that the government will re-examine the various currency reforms studied in the past and establish a complete and feasible system in the shortest possible time so that China's currency can also fully utilize its function of saving the national economy. It is especially hoped that the Chinese people will not simply regard economic control and inflation as novel shortcuts and forget the great foundation of construction!

The Soundness of Finance 184

The seriousness of the country's economic situation and the urgency of treatment have been described above. However, looking back at the current financial situation of the government and the financial organization of society, we cannot help but feel that they are moving in opposite directions. The central government's total annual revenue is over 680 million yuan, while its expenditure is over 828.9 million yuan. The annual deficit is consistently over 140 million yuan, with military spending accounting for the majority. The number of public bonds issued annually, excluding the twenty-first year, is often in the amount of 11 or 120 million yuan. The only funds available to society are absorbed by high-interest public bonds, and everyone sighs and resents the lack of funds for construction and production. Without production funds, how can we seek improvement and advancement in production and achieve a balance of trade? Without economic construction, how can we increase the purchasing power of the people and promote the rise of prices? The issuance volume of Shanghai Chinese banks in the twenty-second year was 454,143,165 yuan, an increase of over 23 million yuan compared to the twenty-first year. The total amount of deposits is estimated to be 210 million yuan, an increase of approximately 10 million yuan compared to last year. In Shanghai alone, six new banks were established, and existing banks added 16 branch offices, all inclined to invest in public bonds and real estate due to a lack of good, high-interest investments. Those who pay attention to business also find that the channels for lending are narrow, and they do not carefully select borrowers' credit and collateral discounts. The unreasonable expansion of credit is becoming more and more serious. Under these unsound financial conditions, if the government sees the rise in public bond prices as a sign of improved government credit and banks see the abundance of idle funds as a symbol of increased social wealth, then there is a great misunderstanding. There is one more fact that deserves attention: the silver reserves of foreign banks are increasing daily. Last year, they accounted for 42.22%, while this year, they account for 50.35%. If the state does not know how to economize on spending, the people's production cannot be improved, exports do not increase, and imports do not decrease, then the trend of cash flowing into foreign banks will become increasingly serious, and the people's wealth will continue to decrease. Who knows if there will be a day when deposits decrease and credit contracts? The difficulty of maintaining public bond prices and the lack of channels for public bond issuance are all expected. This is a cause for deep concern about the future of finance. The remedies are only for the government to substantially reduce military spending, eliminate unnecessary expenditures, reduce the issuance of public bonds, and increase production and construction funds. The financial sector should reduce interest rates, lower costs, and seek the accumulation of strength in preparation for contingencies. At the same time, the government should save 10 or 20 million yuan annually to establish a debt reduction fund, consolidate domestic and foreign debt to establish external credit, and attract foreign investment. On the one hand, establish a central and local harmonized issuance system to achieve the establishment of a currency system and increase currency credit and quantity. Our financial sector has been longing for the soundness of finance for several years, and now there is a real sense of urgency.
